قوله : وحكم الأمر نوعان أداء وهو تسليم عين الواجب بالأمر قضاء وهو تسليم مثل الواجب أمر سے وجوب ثابت ہوتا ہے اس کی دو قسمیں ہیں (۱) وجوب أداء یہ ہے کہ امر سے جو کچھ واجب ہو اس کو بعینہ بلا تغیر و تبدل ادا کرنا۔ علامہ فخر الاسلام وغیرہ نے أداء کی تعریف یہ کی ہے (تسلیم نفس الواجب بالأمر) اس پر اعتراض ہوتا ہے کہ نفس وجوب امر کے ساتھ نہیں ہوتا بلکہ وہ تو وقت کے ساتھ ہوتا ہے۔ جواب اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ (بالأمر) تسلیم کے ساتھ متعلق ہے واجب کے ساتھ متعلق نہیں ہے تو مطلب یہ ہوا کہ تسلیم کرنا یہ امر کے ساتھ متعلق ہے باقی یہ کہ وجوب کس کے ساتھ ہے امر کے ساتھ یا وقت کے ساتھ اس کے بارے میں یہاں کوئی بات نہیں ہوئی بلکہ سکوت ہے۔ (۲) وجوب قضاء یہ ہے کہ مثل واجب کو امر کے ساتھ ادا کرنا " تسليم مثل الواجب بالأمر " نکتہ : بعض لوگوں نے کہا کہ یہاں پر (من عنده) کی قید لگانا چاہیے کیونکہ اگر کوئی شخص آج ظہر کی نماز کل کی ظہر کی نماز کی قضاء ادا کرے تو یہ جائز نہیں ہے۔
His statement: 'And the ruling of the command is of two types: ada' which is delivering the very object of the obligation with the command, and qada' which is delivering the like of the obligation.' From the command, obligation is established. Its two types: (1) Obligation of ada': It is to perform the very thing that becomes obligatory from the command without change or alteration. Imam Fakhr al-Islam and others defined ada' as 'delivering the very object of the obligation with the command.' There is an objection: the very obligation is not with the command but with the time. Answer: The answer is that 'with the command' is attached to 'delivering,' not to the 'obligation.' So the meaning is that delivering is attached to the command. As for whether the obligation is with the command or with time, there is no discussion here; it is silent. (2) Obligation of qada': It is to deliver the like of the obligation with the command: 'delivering the like of the obligation with the command.' Point: Some have said that one should add the condition 'from himself' (min 'indihi) here, because if someone today performs qada' of today's Zuhr prayer for yesterday's Zuhr prayer, it is not valid.
Source pages p. 82

Commentary
This passage is a definition and expansion of two types of obligation arising from a command (amr) in usul al-fiqh. The matn states that the ruling of a command is twofold: ada' (performance) and qada' (make-up). Ada' is performing the exact act commanded, while qada' is performing similar act (like in kind) at a later time. The commentator, likely from a sharh of Nur al-Anwar, explains that obligation is proven by the command. He then clarifies the definition of ada' given by Fakhr al-Islam, which uses 'delivering the very wajib with the command'. An objection arises: since obligation is tied to time (e.g., Zuhr prayer is only obligatory at its time), how can it be 'with the command'? The answer resolves by parsing the Arabic: the phrase 'with the command' qualifies 'delivering', not 'obligation'. Thus the delivery (performance) is associated with the command, while the obligation's attachment (to time or command) is not addressed here. For qada', it is delivering something similar to the wajib, also associated with the command. A note adds that some scholars require the condition 'min 'indihi' (from himself, i.e., on his own initiative, not due to another's order) to avoid cases like performing qada of today's prayer for yesterday's, which would be invalid. This subtly touches on the necessity that qada' must be for a missed obligation, not for a future one.

Key Terms
أداء (adā'): Delivering the very same wajib that is commanded, without change, i.e., performing the obligation on time as commanded.
قضاء (qaḍā'): Delivering the like (mithl) of the wajib, with the command, i.e., performing a similar act at a later time as a make-up for a missed obligation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why did some scholars add the condition 'min `indihi' to the definition of qada'?
A) To ensure qada' is performed at the same time as the missed obligation
B) To prevent performing qada' for a future, not-yet-missed obligation
C) To require that qada' be performed in congregation
D) To make qada' identical in every detail to the original

Key Takeaway
Qada' is a makeup obligation triggered by missing the original; it must be performed after the fact, not anticipatorily.

Types of Hukm al-Amr: Ada' and Qada' Defined
Definition and defense of two types of hukm al-amr: ada' and qada'.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define ada' and qada' as types of hukm al-amr, explain the objections and responses, and apply the definitional distinctions.

Core Idea
Ada' delivers the exact obligation; qada' delivers its like; both are tied to the command, not the time.

This lesson explores the Hanafi usul definitions of ada' (performance) and qada' (make-up) as two types of rulings from a command. We will examine the precise wording of each definition, address an objection regarding the role of time, and understand why certain restrictions are implied rather than stated. This foundational distinction clarifies how obligations relate to commands in Islamic legal theory.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definitions
Read the definitions of ada' and qada' as given in the matn: 'delivering the exact obligated thing by the command' and 'delivering the like of the obligated thing by the command'. Note the key elements: taslim (delivery), 'ayn (exact) vs mithl (like), and bi'l-amr (by the command).
The phrase bi'l-amr is crucial and will be examined in the objection.
2
Analyze the objection to ada'
The objection claims that obligation (wujub) is attached to time, not the command, so the definition is flawed. Identify the mistaken assumption and the Hanafi response: 'by the command' modifies 'delivering', not 'the obligated thing'. This preserves the definition.
Understand that the definition does not claim that the obligation arises from the command alone; it only asserts that the delivery is commanded.
3
Examine the note on qada'
Some scholars suggested adding 'min 'indihi' (from him) to the qada' definition to exclude performing today's Zuhr as qada' for yesterday's. The response says this is implicitly understood and well-known, so no explicit restriction is needed.
This illustrates the principle that in definitions, commonly understood exceptions need not be stated.
4
Derive the key usul principle
From both definitions and responses, extract the principle that 'by the command' relates to the delivery of the act, not to the obligation itself. This clarifies the relationship between the command and the performance.
This principle is foundational for understanding how commands generate obligations.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : وحكم الامر نوعان اداء وهو تسليم عين الواجب بالامر و قضاء وهو تسليم مثل الواجب بالامر  امر سے و جنوب ثابت ہوتا ہے اس کی دو قسمیں ہیں وجوب اداء وجوب قضاء (1) وجوب اداء یہ ہے کہ امر سے جو کچھ واجب ہو اس کو بعینہ بلا تغیر و تبدل ادا کر علامہ فخر الاسلام وغیرہ نے اداء کی تعریف یہ کی ہے (تسلیم نفس الواجب بالامر ) اس پر اعتراض ہوتا ہے کہ نفس وجوب امر کیساتھ نہیں ہوتا بلکہ وہ تو وقت کیساتھ ہوتا ہے۔ جواب اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ ( بالامر ) تسلیم کے ساتھ متعلق ہے واجب کے ساتھ متعلق نہیں ہے تو مطلب یہ ہوا کہ تسلیم کرنا یہ امر کیساتھ متعلق ہے باقی یہ کہ وجوب کس کے ساتھ ہے امر کیساتھ یا وقت کیساتھ اس کے بارے میں یہاں کوئی بات نہیں ہوئی بلکہ سکوت ہے۔ (۲) وجوب قضاء یہ ہے کہ مثل واجب کو امر کیساتھ ادا کرنا " تسليم مثل الواجب بالامر " نکتے ۔ بعض لوگوں نے کہا کہ یہاں پر (من عندہ) کی قید لگانا چاہیے کیونکہ اگر کوئی شخص آج ظہر کی نماز کو کل کی ظہر کی نماز کی قضاء ادا کرے تو یہ جائز نہیں ہے۔ تو اس تصور کو نکالنے کے لئے من عندہ کی قید ہونی چاہیے تھی۔ جواب جواب یہ ہے کہ چونکہ یہ بات التزاما مدلول علیہ اور مشہور تھی اس لئے اس کی قید نہیں لگائی۔ اس مقام پر کئی شبھات اور بھی کئے گئے ہیں جن کو ہم طوالت کے خوف اور عدم فائدہ کی بناء پر ترک کر رہے ہیں۔
He said: The ruling of the command is of two types: ada' (performance), which is delivering the exact obligated thing by the command; and qada' (make-up), which is delivering the like of the obligated thing by the command. From the command, obligation is established, and it has two types: wujub al-ada' and wujub al-qada'. (1) Wujub al-ada': that whatever is obligated by the command, he performs it exactly without change or alteration. Fakhr al-Islam and others defined ada' as 'delivering the exact obligated thing by the command'. Objection: The exact obligation is not attached to the command, but rather it is attached to the time. Answer: The answer is that 'by the command' is related to delivering, not to the obligated. So the meaning is that delivering is related to the command. As for whether the obligation is with the command or with the time, no discussion is made here; it is silent. (2) Wujub al-qada': that one performs the like of the obligated thing by the command. Note: Some said that the restriction 'from him' (min 'indihi) should be added here, because if someone performs today's Zuhr prayer as qada' for yesterday's Zuhr prayer, it is not permissible. So to remove this notion, the restriction 'from him' should have been added. Answer: The answer is that since this matter is implicitly understood and well-known, the restriction was not added. At this point, several other doubts have been raised, which we omit due to fear of length and lack of benefit.
Source pages p. 82

Commentary
This passage is a definition and explanation of the two types of rulings that arise from a command (amr) in Hanafi usul al-fiqh. The author first states the matn: the ruling of the command is of two types — ada' (performance) and qada' (make-up). Ada' is delivering the exact obligated thing as commanded, while qada' is delivering something similar. The commentator then expands, noting that Fakhr al-Islam defined ada' as 'delivering the exact obligated thing by the command.' An objection is raised: obligation is often attached to time, not directly to the command. The response clarifies that the phrase 'by the command' modifies 'delivering,' not the obligated thing; thus the definition remains valid. For qada', the definition is 'delivering the like of the obligated thing by the command.' Some scholars suggested adding the restriction 'from him' (min 'indihi) to exclude cases like performing today's Zuhr as qada' for yesterday's Zuhr, which is invalid. The commentator replies that such a scenario is implicitly excluded by common knowledge, so no explicit restriction is needed. The passage ends by mentioning that other doubts are left aside for brevity.

Key Terms
اداء (adā'): Delivering the exact obligated thing by the command
قضاء (qaḍā'): Delivering the like of the obligated thing by the command
تسليم (taslīm): Delivery or handing over of the obligated act

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) Ada' is done on time, while qada' is done later.
C) Ada' requires intention, while qada' does not.
D) Ada' is for obligatory acts, while qada' is for voluntary acts.

Key Takeaway
Ada' and qada' are distinguished by whether the exact act or its like is delivered, both tied to the command, not the time.

Asl and Khalaf in Hanafi Usul: The Case of Qurbani
Resolving two probabilities about qurbani as original or substitute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi usul concepts of asl and khalaf to identify when a ruling reverts to its original after a substitute condition expires.

Core Idea
A substitute (khalaf) holds during specific conditions; when conditions change, the original (asl) ruling revives.

This passage explores two probabilities regarding the obligation of qurbani (sacrifice) during the Days of Nahr. The author resolves that sacrifice itself is the original ruling during those days, but when the days pass, the original obligation of sadaqa returns. This analysis illustrates the Hanafi usul concept of asl (original) and khalaf (substitute), a key tool for understanding how rulings shift with context.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two probabilities
The passage presents two possibilities: either sacrifice is original (asl) or it is a substitute (khalaf) for charity. Note the textual indicators.
The first probability is that sacrifice itself is the original. The second is that charity was original and sacrifice is a substitute.
2
Understand the reason for substitution
The transfer to sacrifice happened because these days are for hospitality, so meat is appropriate. This is the talil (rationale).
The reason is that these are days of Allah's hospitality, and the best hospitality involves pure meat.
3
Determine the temporal condition
The substitute (sacrifice) applies only during the days of sacrifice. When they expire, we revert to the original (charity).
The text explicitly says: 'as long as the days of sacrifice exist, we say sacrifice is the original. But when the days pass, we revert to the original, which is to give charity.'
4
Apply the principle to another case
Consider how the same asl/khalaf structure might appear in other rulings, such as tayammum replacing wudu temporarily.
In tayammum, the original (wudu) is replaced by a substitute (tayammum) when water is absent. When water becomes available, one reverts to wudu.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
کریگا۔ جواب کا جواب یہ ہے کہ قربانی کے دنوں میں جو قربانی کی جاتی ہے اس میں دو احتمال ہیں پہلا احتمال یہ ہے کہ قربانی کے ایام میں قربانی کرنا ہی اصل ہو ۔ (1) (۲) دوسرا احتمال یہ ہے کہ اصل تو یہ تھا کہ مین شاہ یا اس کی قیمت کا صدقہ کیا جائے اور قربانی کرنا اس کا خلف ہے اور اصل کو چھوڑ کر خلف کی طرف انتقال اس لئے کیا گیا کہ یہ دن اللہ تعالی کی مہمانی کے دن ہیں اور مہمانی پاک گوشت کیساتھ ہوگی جو کہ بہترین کھانا ہے تو جب تک قربانی کے ایام موجود ہونگے تو ہم کہیں گے قربانی کرنا اصل ہے لیکن جب قربانی کے ایام فوت ہو گئے تو اصل کی طرف رجوع کرینگے اور وہ یہ ہے کہ صدقہ کیا جائے پھر اگر دوسرے سال کی عید آ بھی گئی تو ہم اس اصل کو بھی چھوڑیں گے۔
He will do. The answer to the answer is that sacrifice performed on the days of sacrifice has two probabilities. The first probability is that performing the sacrifice during the days of sacrifice is the original (asl). The second probability is that the original was to give charity of a goat or its value, and the sacrifice is a substitute (khalaf) for it. The transfer from the original to the substitute was made because these are the days of Allah's hospitality, and hospitality is with pure meat, which is the best food. So as long as the days of sacrifice exist, we say sacrifice is the original. But when the days of sacrifice pass, we revert to the original, which is to give charity. Then if the next year's Eid comes, we will also leave this original.
Source pages p. 90

Commentary
This passage is a textual analysis of the ruling on qurbani (sacrifice) on the Days of Nahr. The author presents two probabilities: either sacrifice itself is the original obligation during those days, or the original obligation is to give sadaqa (charity) of a goat or its value, and sacrifice is a substitute due to the hospitality aspect. The preferred view according to the text is that during the days, sacrifice is the original, but when the days expire, we revert to the original obligation of sadaqa. If the next year arrives, we again prioritize sacrifice. This illustrates the Hanafi usul principle that an original ruling may be temporarily replaced by a substitute (khalaf) in specific contexts.

Key Terms
قربانی (qurbani): The ritual sacrifice of an animal on the days of Eid al-Adha.
اصل (asl): The original legal obligation from which one may deviate to a substitute in specific circumstances.
خلف (khalaf): A substitute that replaces the original ruling under certain conditions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling when the days of sacrifice pass?
A) The sacrifice must be made up the next year.
B) One must give sadaqa (charity) of a goat or its value.
C) The obligation is waived entirely.
D) One must fast instead.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi usul of asl and khalaf shows that a substitute ruling is temporally bound to its condition; once the condition ends, the original ruling resumes.

Types of Qada in Huquq al-Ibad and the Priority of Mithl Suri
Defining types of qada in huquq al-ibad

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the three types of qada in huquq al-ibad and apply the Hanafi principle that mithl suri takes precedence over mithl ma'nawi.

Core Idea
When a property right is lost, the substitute (qada) is a like (mithl) if possible; otherwise value; for life and limbs, it is monetary (diya).

In Hanafi usul, qada (substitute fulfillment) arises when the original act or object cannot be performed or returned. This passage from al-Nur al-Anwar clarifies three kinds of qada in the sphere of huquq al-ibad (rights of people): returning an exact like, monetary compensation for items without a like, and a hybrid resembling performance. A key principle emerges: mithl suri (formal like) is given priority over mithl ma'nawi (value).

Guided Path
1
Identify the three types of qada
Read the passage and note each type: qada bi mithl ma'qul (rational like), qada bi mithl ghayr ma'qul (irrational like), and qada mushabih bi al-ada (similar to performance).
These correspond to different categories of huquq al-ibad.
2
Examine the first type: qada bi mithl ma'qul
This applies when a misappropriated item has a mithl suri (formal like). The usurper must return the mithl, not value, as long as the mithl is available.
Mithl suri means an identical or exactly equivalent item.
3
Examine the second type: qada bi mithl ghayr ma'qul
This applies to life and limbs. Since they have no mithl, the substitute is monetary (diya), even though there is no rational similarity.
The 'irrational like' here means compensation is by value, not by an actual like.
4
Examine the third type: qada mushabih bi al-ada
In a marriage contract with a non-specific slave, if the husband gives value, it is qada but function like ada because it settles the dispute based on quality/price.
The wife is compelled to accept value because it resolves the uncertainty about the slave's grade.
5
Apply the principle: mithl suri over mithl ma'nawi
The passage ends by stating that mithl suri takes precedence. This means if the original item has a mithl, that must be given; only when impossible do we revert to value.
Imam Abu Hanifa built furu' on this, e.g., in qisas and diya for intentional harm.

قوله : ومنها ضمان المغصوب بالمثل وهو السابق او بالقيمة الخ قضاء بمثل معقول کی مثال : حقوق العباد میں قضا بمثل المعقول کی مثال یہ ہے کہ غاصب نے کوئی چیز غصب کرلی پھر اس کو ہلاک کردیا تو اگر وہ چیز ملی تھی تو غاصب پر اس کی مثل کی منمان دینا واجب ہوگا۔ لیکن مثل صوری کیسا تھ ضمان دینا یہ مشکل کامل ہے۔ اور مشکل معنوی یعنی قیمت کیسا تھ ضمان دینا یہ شل قاصر ہے تو جب تک مثل کامل پائی جاتی ہے اس وقت تک مثل قاصر کی طرف رجوع نہیں کریں گے۔ قوله : وضمان النفس والاطراف بالمال قضاء بمثل غیر معقول کی مثال : حقوق العباد قضاء بمثل غیر معقول کی مثال یہ ہے کہ اگر کسی شخص کو خطاء " قتل کر دیا یا خطاء اس کے اعضاء کاٹ دیئے جائیں تو مجرم پر اس کی دیت اور اعضاء کا ضمان لازم ہے حالا نکہ انسانی جان اور انسانی اعضاء اور مال کے درمیان کوئی مماثلت سمجھ میں نہیں آتی۔ قوله : واداء القيمة فيما اذا تزوج على عبد بغير عينه حتى تجبر على القبول كما لو أتاها بالمسمى قضاء مشابه بالا داء کی مثال : قضاء مشابہ بالاداء کی مثال یہ ہے کہ اگر کسی آدمی نے عورت کیساتھ شادی کی غیر معین غلام کو بدنے ہیں تو اگر دار پر درمیانے درجے کا غلام خرید کر بیوی کو دیدے تو ادا ہوگئی اور اگر اس بر کی قیمت دے دے تو یہ قضاء ہوگئی لیکن اداء کے معنی میں ہوگی اس لئے کہ میاں بیوی کے درمیان غلام کے بارے میں جو جھگڑا ہو سکتا ہے اس کو ختم کرنے کا معیار قیمت ہے۔ کیونکہ جو اعلیٰ قیمت والا غلام ہو گا ہ و اعنی ہوگا اور جو کم قیمت والا ہو گا وہ ارنی ہوگا اور جو درمیانی قیمت والا ہو گا وہ متو ا ہوگا یا اقیت کا دینا بھی ادا کے معنی میں ہے۔ لہذا عورت کو قیمت کے قبول کرنے پر مجبور کیا جائیگا۔ نک مثل صوری مثل معنوی سے مقدم ہے اس پر امام صاحب دو تفریعیں اٹھاتے ہیں۔ مثل صوری مثل معنوی پر مقدم ہے۔ قوله : وعلى هذا قال ابو حنيفة في القطع ثم القتل عمداً للولى فعلهما
He said: 'Among them is the guarantee of the misappropriated object by its like (mithl), which is the precedent, or by its value, etc.' An example of qada by a rational like (mithl ma'qul): In rights of people, an example is that a usurper took an object and destroyed it. If the object had a mithl (like), it is wajib for the usurper to give a mithl. But giving mithl suri (formal like) is difficult; giving mithl ma'nawi (effective like) i.e. value is less difficult. So as long as the complete mithl is available, we do not revert to the deficient mithl. He said: 'And the guarantee of life and limbs by wealth.' An example of qada by an irrational like: In rights of people, if someone kills a person by mistake or cuts his limbs by mistake, the criminal is liable for blood money (diya) and guarantee of limbs, even though there is no similarity between human life/limbs and wealth. He said: 'And fulfilling the value when a man marries on a non-specific slave so that she is compelled to accept, as if he brings her the named one.' An example of qada similar to ada: If a man marries a woman on a non-specific slave, and then the husband purchases a medium-grade slave and gives it to the wife, it is ada (performance). If he gives its value, it is qada, but in the sense of ada, because the criterion to settle the potential dispute between husband and wife regarding the slave is the value. For a high-value slave is 'ali (high), a low-value one is arkhasi (cheaper), and a medium one is mutawassit (average). Giving value is also in the sense of ada. Hence the woman is compelled to accept the value. Now: 'The mithl suri takes precedence over mithl ma'nawi.' On this, Imam (Abu Hanifa) raises two furu' (branches). 'The mithl suri takes precedence over mithl ma'nawi.' He said: 'On this, Abu Hanifa said regarding cutting then intentional killing: the guardian (wali) has the right to do both.'
Source pages p. 90

Commentary
This passage defines three types of qada (substitute judgments) in the context of huquq al-ibad (rights of people). First, qada bi mithl ma'qul: when a misappropriated item has a mithl suri (similar in form), that must be returned; only if that is impossible does one revert to value (mithl ma'nawi). Second, qada bi mithl ghayr ma'qul: for life and limbs, since they have no mithl, the substitute is monetary compensation (diya). Third, qada mushabih bi al-ada: in a marriage contract with a non-specific slave, if the husband gives a slave of average value, it counts as ada (performance); if he gives its value, it is qada but functionally similar to ada because the dispute is settled by value. The passage ends by stating the principle that mithl suri is preferred over mithl ma'nawi, and Imam Abu Hanifa derives two furu' from this (the first of which is mentioned: in intentional cutting of limbs before murder, the guardian may choose either qisas or diya).

Key Terms
قضاء (qada): A substitute act that fulfills an obligation when the original is impossible or replaced by a legal ruling.
مثل صوری (mithl suri): A like in form, i.e. an identical item or its exact equivalent.
ضمان (daman): Liability to compensate for damage or loss.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the example of marriage on a non-specific slave, why is the woman compelled to accept the value?
A) Because value is higher than the slave's worth.
B) Because value resolves the potential dispute about quality.
C) Because the slave is not present.
D) Because the husband is poor.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi usul of qada teaches that when a right is lost, the substitute must match the original's nature: a like item (mithl suri) if available, otherwise value; for life and limbs, only monetary compensation applies.

The Commanded Act Must Be Good (Husn al-Ma'mur Bih)
States the usul principle that a commanded act must inherently be good because the Commander is wise.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi usul principle that a commanded act must be good, explain its rational proof, and contrast it with the Shafi'i position.

Core Idea
A wise Commander cannot command evil; therefore every commanded act is intrinsically good.

At the heart of Hanafi usul is the conviction that God is wise (hakim). This lesson explores a direct implication: any act He commands must be good (hasan). This principle shapes how Hanafi jurists reason about divine commands and opens the door for rational judgment in ijtihad. We will examine the proof and contrast it with the Shafi'i view that only revelation defines good and evil.

Guided Path
1
State the Principle
Identify the core claim: the commanded act (ma'mur bihi) must have the attribute of goodness (husn). This is presented as a necessary (daruri) quality.
2
Identify the Proof
The text gives the reason: 'because the Commander is wise' (al-amir hakim). This is a rational proof (dalil aqli).
3
Explain the Rational Link
A wise being cannot command evil. Therefore, the attribute of goodness is inseparable from the commanded act. This link is self-evident to reason.
Hanafi: reason can directly perceive this necessity.
4
Contrast the Shafi'i View
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that good and evil are determined solely by Shariah, not by reason. Thus, the commanded act's goodness is a revealed quality, not a rational one.
This is a methodological difference (ikhtilaf fi al-usul).
5
Note the Practical Consequence
In Hanafi thought, if reason judges an act to be good and no revelation prohibits it, the act can be assumed permissible (ibaha). For Shafi'is, only revelation establishes permissibility.
This affects istihsan and the role of reason in ijtihad.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : ولا بد للما موربه من صفة الحسن ضرورة أن
الأمر حكيم
ماموریہ کے لئے صفت حسن ضروری ہے
امر بہ کیلئے حسن کی صفت کا ہونا ضر ہبری ہے اس لئے کہ امر حکیم ذات کا حکم ہے اور حکیم
کبھی بھی بری بات کا حکم نہیں دیتا۔
مگر امام شافعی فرماتے ہیں کہ حسن اور قبیح کا فیصلہ کرنے والی شریعت
His saying: 'And the commanded act must have the attribute of goodness, necessarily because the Commander is wise.' The commanded act must have the attribute of goodness, because the command is from a Wise Being, and a wise being never commands an evil thing. But Imam Shafi'i says that the decider of good and evil is the Shariah.
Source pages p. 95

Commentary
This passage introduces a core usul principle: the act commanded (ma'mur bihi) must be intrinsically good (hasan) because the Commander (al-amir) is wise (hakim). This is a rational argument: a wise being cannot command evil; thus every divine command is good. Imam Shafi'i holds that good and evil are determined by revelation (Shariah), not by reason. This is a classic dispute between the Hanafi (rationalist) and Ash'ari/Shafi'i positions.

Key Terms
حسن (husn): Goodness or praiseworthiness of an act, discernible by reason.
قبيح (qubh): Evil or blameworthy act.
حكيم (hakim): Wise; attribute of God.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi usul principle in this passage, why must the commanded act be good?
A) Because the Quran says so.
B) Because the Commander is wise.
C) Because the community agreed.
D) Because the Prophet said so.

Key Takeaway
The commanded act must be good because the Commander is wise; this Hanafi principle grounds the role of reason in ijtihad and distinguishes the school from the Shafi'i approach.

Liability of Retracting Witnesses in Divorce Testimony: The Hanafi Principle of Non-Compensability of Marital Rights
Fiqh example illustrating liability of witnesses who retract testimony on divorce after consummation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle that loss of marital rights (milk al-nikah) after consummation is not compensable via witness retraction, and distinguish the scenario before consummation where half mahr is claimed.

Core Idea
After consummation, mahr is fixed by intercourse, not divorce; the loss of marital intimacy has no monetary equivalent.

This passage from a Hanafi commentary illustrates a key rule in the law of witness retraction (ruju' al-shuhud). It distinguishes between two scenarios: testimony of divorce after consummation and before consummation. The ruling hinges on whether the loss suffered by the husband is quantifiable in shariah. Understanding this reasoning deepens your grasp of daman (tort liability) and the unique status of marital rights (milk al-nikah) in Hanafi fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Outline the two scenarios
State the two cases discussed: testimony of divorce after consummation and before consummation. Note the different rulings on witness liability.
The passage uses 'after consummation' as the default and then clarifies the opposite case.
2
Analyze the after-consummation ruling
Understand why the husband cannot claim compensation: mahr already wajib due to intercourse, and the loss of bud' has no mithl. The commentary explains that bud' cannot be valued in property except in marriage by necessity.
The key term is 'mithl' – the lost right has no comparable monetary value.
3
Analyze the before-consummation ruling
Understand why witnesses are liable for half mahr: before consummation, mahr could fall away (e.g., due to excuses). The testimony made it certain, so witnesses are responsible for that half.
This shows that liability attaches when the testimony creates a new, certain obligation.
4
Extract the usul principle
From this reasoning, derive the principle: For a retracting witness to be liable, the loss must be quantifiable in shariah (have a mithl). Loss of marital rights after consummation is not quantifiable.
This is a talil that illustrates how the Hanafi school determines daman in tort.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وملك النكاح لا يضمن بالشهادة بالطلاق بعد الدخول ای اصول پر تیسری تفریع یہ اٹھاتے ہیں کہ اگر دو آدمیوں نے گواہی دی کہ فلاں نے دخول کے بعد بیوی کو تین طلاقیں دیدیں ہیں اور قاضی نے مہر کے ادا کرنے اور افتراق کا فیصلہ کر دیا ہے پھر گواہوں نے اپنی گواہی سے رجوع کر لیا کہ اس نے طلاقیں نہیں دی تھیں ۔ تو ہمارے نزدیک شوہر ان گواہوں سے کسی قسم کا مطالبہ نہیں کرے گا اس لئے کہ مہر تو شوہر پر جماع (ولی) کی وجہ سے واجب ہو چکا تھا خواہ وہ طلاق دیتا ہو یا نہ دیتا ہو ان گواہوں کی وجہ سے شوہر کو صرف یہ نقصان ہوا کہ ملک بضعہ فوت ہو گئی ہے لیکن بضعہ کا کوئی مثل نہیں کیونکہ اگر طعہ کا مثل بضعہ کو بناتے ہیں تو یہ حرام ہے اور اگر بضعہ کا مثل مال کو بناتے ہے تو یہ جائز نہیں اس لئے کہ بضعہ کے بدلے میں مال ضرورت کی بنا پر صرف نکاح میں دیا جاتا ہے۔ نکاح کے علاوہ کہیں بھی مال کار ینا سیج نہیں ۔ جماع کی قید ہم نے اس لئے لگائی کہ اگر گواہوں نے گواہی دی کہ اس نے جماع سے پہلے طلاق دی تو اس صورت میں گواہ نصف مہر کے ضامن ہونگے اسلئے کہ جماع سے پہلے احتمال تھا۔ کہ شاید کسی عذر کی وجہ سے مہر ساقط ہو جائے مگر طلاق کی گواہی کی وجہ سے نصف مہر مؤکد ہو گیا اس لئے اس نصف مہر کا مطالبہ ان گواہوں سے کیا جائے گا۔
And ownership of nikah is not guaranteed by testimony of divorce after consummation. This is the third corollary on the principles: If two men testify that a certain person gave three divorces to his wife after consummation, and the judge ruled for payment of mahr and separation, then the witnesses retract their testimony saying that he did not give divorce. Then according to us, the husband cannot demand anything from these witnesses because the mahr had become obligatory upon the husband due to intercourse (consummation) whether he gave divorce or not. (The only loss to the husband due to these witnesses is that the ownership of the vulva [right to sexual intimacy] has been lost. But the vulva has no equivalent because if one makes the equivalent of the vulva [as something comparable], that is prohibited; and if one makes the equivalent of property [for the vulva], that is not permissible because property is given in exchange for the vulva only out of necessity in marriage. Outside of marriage, taking property [for it] is not permissible.) We have mentioned the restriction of intercourse because if the witnesses testified that he gave divorce before intercourse, then in that case the witnesses are liable for half the mahr, because before intercourse there was a possibility that the mahr might fall due to some excuse, but due to the testimony of divorce, half the mahr became confirmed; therefore, that half mahr can be claimed from these witnesses.
Source pages p. 95

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the matn statement 'And ownership of nikah is not guaranteed by testimony of divorce after consummation.' It presents a fiqh ruling regarding witnesses who retract their testimony. The key points: (1) After consummation, mahr is already wajib on the husband due to the act of intercourse itself, independently of divorce. Therefore, if witnesses retract, the husband loses nothing compensable because the loss of marital rights (bid') cannot be quantified in monetary terms. (2) If the divorce was testified before consummation, then the witnesses become liable for half the mahr because before consummation there was a possibility that mahr could be waived; the testimony confirmed it. This distinction is based on the Hanafi principle that bid' has no mithl (equivalent) in property law, except in the context of marriage where mahr is given by necessity.

Key Terms
ملک النکاح (milk al-nikah): Ownership of the marriage contract, giving the husband the right to sexual intimacy with his wife.
بضعہ (bud'ah): The vulva or female genitalia, representing the object of marital intimacy.
مثل (mithl): Equivalent or comparable thing in value or kind, used in compensation (daman).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi ruling in this passage, why are witnesses who retract their testimony about divorce after consummation not liable to the husband?
A) Because the husband still has the right to remarry his wife
B) Because the mahr was already obligatory due to consummation, and the loss of marital rights has no monetary equivalent
C) Because the witnesses were coerced
D) Because the husband did not suffer any loss

Key Takeaway
After consummation, witnesses who retract divorce testimony are not liable because mahr is already owed due to intercourse, and marital rights have no monetary equivalent in Hanafi law.

Husn in the Commanded Act: Definition and Classification
Usul definition and classification of husn

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define husn li-aynihi and husn li-ghayrihi, and distinguish the three subcategories of husn li-aynihi as presented in the Hanafi usul tradition.

Core Idea
The commanded act must be good because the Commander is Wise; this goodness is either inherent (husn li-aynihi) or acquired (husn li-ghayrihi).

Before we examine the detailed classification of commanded acts, we must first understand why every command from the Wise Lawgiver must inherently be good. This passage from Noor al-Anwar establishes that foundational principle and then introduces the two types of goodness: inherent and acquired. This distinction is critical for understanding how Hanafi usul frames obligation and permission.

Guided Path
1
Establish the necessity of husn
Identify the core assertion: the commanded act must possess the attribute of goodness. The proof is that the Commander (Allah) is Hakim (Wise), and Wisdom precludes commanding evil. This is the talil (rational basis) for the claim.
The Hanafi argument uses the attribute of Wisdom as the operative cause (illa).
2
Recognize the usul dispute
The text notes the disagreement: Hanafis hold that both reason and Shariah determine good and evil; Imam al-Shafi'i restricts this to Shariah alone; the Mu'tazila restrict it to reason alone. Understand that the Hanafi position is a middle path that gives reason a role but does not exclude revelation.
This dispute is foundational to many derived rulings (thurat al-khilaf).
3
Distinguish husn li-aynihi and husn li-ghayrihi
The passage divides the commanded act into two categories: (1) good in itself (husn li-aynihi) – goodness is intrinsic to the act; (2) good due to something else (husn li-ghayrihi) – goodness is acquired from an external factor (e.g., a command). Note that this lesson focuses on the first category.
Husn li-ghayrihi is introduced here but not detailed; it will be covered in subsequent lessons.
4
Analyze the three subcategories of husn li-aynihi
Husn li-aynihi is further divided: (a) acts whose goodness is never dropped (tasdiq – affirmation of faith, because gratitude to the Benefactor is rational obligation); (b) acts whose goodness may be dropped due to excuse (salah – dropped during menstruation); (c) acts annexed to the above but similar to what is good by something else (the text cuts off, but this likely refers to acts that are good due to a reason taken from another act, e.g., wudu without intention?).
The third category is incomplete in the source; classical commentaries expand on it.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : ولا بد للما موربه من صفة الحسن ضرورة أن الأمر حكيم ماموریہ کے لئے صفت حسن ضروری ہے مامور بہ کیلئے حسن کی صفت کا ہونا ضر ہبری ہے اس لئے کہ امر حکیم ذات کا حکم ہے اور حکیم کبھی بھی بری بات کا حکم نہیں دیتا۔ مگر امام شافعی فرماتے ہیں کہ حسن اور قبیح کا فیصلہ کرنے والی شریعت ہے عقل کو اس میں کوئی دخل نہیں ہے لیکن معتزلہ کہتے ہیں کہ حسن اور قبیح کا فیصلہ کر نیوالی عقل ہے شریعت کا اس میں کوئی دخل نہیں۔ قوله : وهو اما أن يكون بعينه وهو اما أن لا يقبل السقوط أو يقبله أو يكون ملحقاً بهذا القسم لكنه مشابه لما حسن المعنى في غيره كالتصديق والصلوة والزكوة مامور بہ کی باعتبار حسن تقسیم حسن کے اعتبار سے مامور بہ کی دو قسمیں ہیں۔ (۱) حسن لعينه (۲) حسن لغيره حسن العینہ کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ بغیر کسی واسطے کے مامور بہ کی ذات میں حسن ہو۔ پھر اس کی تین قسمیں ہیں : (۱) اول یہ کہ وہ حسن مامور بہ سے کبھی بھی ساقط نہ ہوتا ہو جیسے تصدیق کہ تصدیق کر نا کسی حالت میں بھی ساقط نہیں ہو سکتا اور تصدیق حسن لعینہ اس لئے ہے کیونکہ منعم کا شکر ادا کرنا عقل کے اعتبار سے بھی واجب ہے۔ (۲) دوسری قسم یہ ہے کہ کسی عذر کی وجہ سے اس کا حسن کبھی کبھی ساقط ہو جائے جیسا کہ نماز یہ حیض و نفاس کی صورت میں ساقط ہو جاتی ہے۔ (۳) تیسری قسم یہ ہے کہ معنی کے اعتبار سے وہ الحق ہو حسن لعینہ کے ساتھ اور مشابہ عموحسن
He said: And it is necessary for the commanded act to have the attribute of goodness, necessarily because the Commander is Wise. The commanded act must have the attribute of goodness because the command is from a Wise Being, and a Wise Being never commands an evil thing. But Imam al-Shafi'i says that it is the Shariah that decides what is good and evil; reason has no role in it. But the Mu'tazila say that it is reason that decides good and evil; Shariah has no role in it. He said: And it is either [good] in itself, and it either does not admit of being dropped or admits it, or is annexed to this category but similar to what is good in meaning in other things, like tasdiq (affirmation), salah, and zakah. Division of the commanded act with respect to goodness: With respect to goodness, the commanded act is of two types: (1) Husn li-aynihi (good in itself) and (2) Husn li-ghayrihi (good due to something else). The meaning of husn li-aynihi is that goodness is in the essence of the commanded act without any intermediary. Then it is of three types: (1) First, that its goodness is never dropped from the commanded act, like tasdiq (affirmation of faith); tasdiq cannot be dropped in any state, and tasdiq is husn li-aynihi because gratitude to the Benefactor is obligatory even according to reason. (2) Second type: that its goodness is sometimes dropped due to an excuse, like salah which is dropped in the case of hayd (menstruation) and nifas (postpartum bleeding). (3) Third type: that in meaning it is attached to husn li-aynihi and is similar to general goodness.
Source pages p. 96

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the matn statement 'And it is necessary for the commanded act to have the attribute of goodness.' It begins by establishing that the commanded act (ma'mur bihi) must be good (hasan) because the Commander (Allah) is Hakim (Wise), and a wise being does not command evil. The commentary then presents a key usul dispute: Hanafis hold that both reason and revelation determine good and evil (husn wa qubh); Imam Shafi'i holds that only Shariah determines it, while the Mu'tazila hold that only reason determines it. The Hanafi position is that reason can perceive the goodness of certain acts (like gratitude to a benefactor), but Shariah confirms and details them. The passage then divides the commanded act in terms of goodness into two main categories: husn li-aynihi (good in itself) and husn li-ghayrihi (good due to something else). Husn li-aynihi is further divided into three subcategories: (1) Acts whose goodness is never dropped, such as tasdiq (affirmation of faith), because it is rationally obligatory to thank the Benefactor. (2) Acts whose goodness may be dropped due to a valid excuse, such as salah being dropped during menstruation and postpartum bleeding. (3) Acts that are annexed to the previous category but are similar to something that is good in meaning due to something else; the text cuts off describing this third type, but it likely refers to acts that are not inherently good but become so by association (like husn li-ghayrihi?). The division illustrates that different types of commanded acts have different degrees of necessity and conditions.

Key Terms
حسن لعينه (husn li-aynihi): Goodness inherent in the essence of an act, not derived from an external factor.
حسن لغيره (husn li-ghayrihi): Goodness that accrues to an act due to an external factor, not from its own essence.
تصدیق (tasdiq): Affirmation of faith, belief in Allah and His Messenger.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is an example of an act whose goodness is never dropped (la yuqbal al-suqut)?
A) Salah (prayer)
B) Zakah (alms)
C) Tasdiq (affirmation of faith)
D) Fasting in Ramadan

Key Takeaway
The commanded act must be good; this goodness is either inherent (husn li-aynihi) or acquired (husn li-ghayrihi), and the former includes acts whose obligation is never dropped, like tasdiq.

Hasan li-Ghayrihi: Definition, Types, and Examples
Defining and dividing hasan li-ghayrihi with examples

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define hasan li-ghayrihi, distinguish its three types, and apply the Hanafi framework to classify the moral value of commanded acts.

Core Idea
An act's goodness may come from an external purpose, not its intrinsic nature—this is hasan li-ghayrihi.

In Hanafi usul al-fiqh, the moral value of commanded acts is not always intrinsic. Some acts are good because of an external factor (ghayr). This passage defines hasan li-ghayrihi, outlines its three types, and provides classic examples like wudu and jihad. Understanding this distinction is crucial for analyzing why certain outwardly burdensome acts become praiseworthy in Islamic law.

Guided Path
1
Recall the distinction between hasan li-aynihi and hasan li-ghayrihi
Start by remembering that hasan li-aynihi is good in itself (e.g., iman), while hasan li-ghayrihi is good due to an external factor. This sets the foundation for the three types.
The passage opens with examples of hasan li-aynihi (zakat, fasting, hajj) to contrast with the coming discussion.
2
Identify the external factor (ghayr) in each example
For each commanded act, pinpoint what external good attaches. For wudu, the ghayr is prayer; for jihad, it is elevating Allah's word; for funeral prayer, it is fulfilling the right of the deceased. The type depends on whether the act itself realizes that external purpose.
The external factor must be a valid Islamic objective (maslahah).
3
Categorize the act into one of three types
Apply the three-type division: Type 1: the commanded act does not itself fulfill the external (e.g., wudu does not fulfill prayer). Type 2: the act does fulfill the external (e.g., jihad realizes elevating Allah's word). Type 3: goodness comes from a condition of the act (e.g., ability/qudra), which some consider a separate category.
The passage follows al-Bazdawi in treating the third type as independent, though many scholars consider it merely a condition.
4
Recognize the scholarly debate on the third type
Note that the majority view does not count the third type as independent because ability (qudra) is a condition for every act. Al-Bazdawi's view, included here, treats it separately. This reflects an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.
The author (matn) follows al-Bazdawi, indicating the adopted position in this text.
5
Apply the framework to new examples
Practice by analyzing other commanded acts from fiqh (e.g., ghusl, zakat distribution) and determine which type of hasan li-ghayrihi applies. This builds skill in classifying moral value.
Always identify the external factor first, then see if the act itself achieves it.

Source Text

دوسری قسم کی مثال جہاد ہے کہ فی نفسہ جہاد اللہ کے بندوں کو عذاب دینا، انہیں جان سے مارنا، ان کے گھر بارا جاڑنا ، اور فصلیں نذرآتش کرنا ہے لیکن اس میں حسن آ گیا اعلاء كلمة الله کیوجہ سے اور اعلاء کلمۃ اللہ صرف جہاد سے ادا ہو گا اس کے لئے کسی الگ فعل ( غیر ) کی ضرورت نہیں۔ اسی قسم میں حدود اور قصاص بھی شامل ہیں کہ قصاص اور حدود نی نفسہ تو بندوں کو تکلیف دینا ہے لیکن اس میں حسن آ گیا لوگوں کو گنا ہوں سے روکنے کی وجہ ہے کہ سیا اجرة للناس ہیں۔ اسی طرح نماز جنازہ بھی اس قسم کی مثال ہے فی نفسہ یہ بتوں کی عبادت کے مشابہ ہے لیکن اس میں حسن آیا ہے مسلمان کے حق کی ادائیگی کی وجہ سے۔
یہ ساری مثالیں اس حسن لغیرہ کی ہیں جس میں مامور بہ کے ادا کرنے سے غیر خود بخود
Lastly, together with it, like Zakat: outwardly, giving Zakat is wasting wealth, but goodness comes into it due to fulfilling the need of the poor, which is beloved to Allah, and the poor's being needy is not by his own choice but created by Allah. Second example: similarly, fasting in itself is keeping oneself hungry, but goodness comes into it due to overcoming the commanding self (nafs ammara), and the commanding self is created by Allah. Third example: similarly, Hajj in itself is travel and tourism, wasting money, distancing oneself from relatives and friends, and running about, but goodness comes into it due to the honor of the Kaaba, and the Kaaba's honor is given by Allah. So they are good in themselves (hasanah li-'aynihā).
His statement: 'Or due to other (li-ghayrihi):' and it is either that it is not fulfilled by the act commanded itself, or it is fulfilled, or the goodness is in its condition after it was good in meaning in itself or attached to it, like wudu, jihad, and the ability (qudra) by which the servant can perform what is obligatory upon him.
Definition of حسن لغیرہ (goodness due to another): That commanded act in which goodness comes due to an external factor is called حسن لغیرہ.
It has three types:
Division of حسن لغیرہ:
(1) First type: That the external (ghayr) is not fulfilled by performing the commanded act itself.
(2) Second type: That the external is fulfilled by performing the commanded act.
(3) Third type: That there is goodness in the commanded act due to goodness in its condition; by condition is meant ability (qudra), because Allah does not burden a soul beyond its capacity, as He said: 'Allah does not charge a soul except with its capacity' (2:286).
Page 97
The majority did not consider this third type as an independent category, but rather it is a condition for the other two, because having ability is necessary for every commanded act. The author (matn), following Allama Fakhr al-Islam al-Bazdawi, mentioned it as an independent category.
Whether it is حسن لعینہ (goodness in itself) or attached to حسن لعینہ, due to the condition of ability, it becomes حسن لغیرہ as well. And حسن لغیرہ becomes حسن لغیرہ in two respects: for example, wudu: one goodness is due to prayer, as it is the key to prayer and a means to prayer, and another goodness is due to being a condition for ability.
Clarification with examples of the three types:
Among these three types, the example of the first type is wudu: in itself, wudu is wasting water and time or gaining cleanliness and coolness. But goodness comes into it due to prayer, and prayer is not fulfilled only by performing wudu; rather, it has to be performed separately. So, the first type of حسن لغیرہ: by performing it, the external (ghayr) due to which goodness came is not fulfilled.
The example of the second type is jihad: in itself, jihad is tormenting Allah's servants, killing them, destroying their homes and property, and burning crops, but goodness comes into it due to elevating the word of Allah, and elevating the word of Allah is fulfilled only by jihad; no separate act (ghayr) is needed for it. Similarly, hudud (prescribed punishments) and qisas (retaliation) are included in this type: qisas and hudud in themselves are afflicting pain upon servants, but goodness comes into them due to preventing people from sins, because they are a deterrent for people. Similarly, the funeral prayer is an example of this type: in itself, it resembles the worship of idols, but goodness comes into it due to fulfilling the right of a Muslim.
All these examples are of that حسن لغیرہ in which, by performing the commanded act, the external (ghayr) is automatically...
Source pages p. 97

Commentary
This passage is from a Hanafi usul al-fiqh commentary, expanding on the definition of حسن لغیرہ (goodness derived from another). It begins by giving examples of حسن لعینہ (goodness in itself) from the previous discussion: Zakat, fasting, and Hajj are outwardly burdensome but become good due to divine attributes embedded in the actions. Then it transitions to the definition and division of حسن لغیرہ. The author explains that حسن لغیرہ is goodness that arises from an external factor (ghayr), not from the intrinsic nature of the act. Three types are identified: (1) The commanded act does not itself fulfill the external factor (e.g., wudu does not fulfill prayer; prayer is separate). (2) The commanded act does fulfill the external factor (e.g., jihad itself elevates Allah's word). (3) Goodness in the commanded act due to its condition (ability), which some scholars consider a separate type. The text then provides examples: wudu for type 1, jihad (and hudud, qisas, funeral prayer) for type 2. The third type is debated; the author follows al-Bazdawi in making it independent, while the majority consider it a condition for the other types. The commentary demonstrates the Hanafi approach of categorizing acts based on the source of their moral value.

Key Terms
حسن لعینہ (hasan li-'aynihi): Goodness that is intrinsic to the act itself, not dependent on an external factor.
حسن لغیرہ (hasan li-ghayrihi): Goodness that accrues to an act from an external factor (ghayr), making the act commendable despite its apparent harm.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Jihad
B) Wudu
C) Zakat
D) Hajj

Key Takeaway
Hasan li-ghayrihi classifies commanded acts as good due to an external purpose, divided into three types based on whether the act itself fulfills that purpose.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling

Definition and Two Types of Power (Qudra) as Condition for Obligation
Explanation of qudra as condition for taklīf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define qudra as a condition for taklīf, distinguish its two types, and apply the concept of absolute power to determine obligation.

Core Idea
Power for obligation is pre-existing capacity, not the ability concurrent with the act.

In Hanafi usul, the obligation (taklīf) depends on the mukallaf's ability to perform the commanded act. This lesson clarifies that the relevant power is not the power that exists during the act but the pre-existing capacity provided by sound limbs and available means. The text then divides this power into two types, focusing on absolute power (qudra muṭlaqa) as the minimal condition for every command.

Guided Path
1
Identify the key term and its definition
Locate the term 'qudra' in the text and note that it is defined as 'power in the sense of safety of means and instruments and soundness of limbs' that exists before the act.
This pre-existing power is distinct from the power that arises during the act itself.
2
Contrast pre-existing power with concurrent power
Understand why concurrent power cannot be the basis for obligation: it occurs after the act begins, so it cannot be a condition for initiating the obligation.
The text explicitly rejects 'the power with which the act occurs' as the intended meaning.
3
Apply the concept to examples
Analyze the examples given: wudu requires the presence of water (pre-existing means), and zakah requires ownership of nisab. In their absence, obligation is substituted or waived.
This demonstrates how pre-existing power is a practical condition for obligation.
4
Differentiate the two types of power
Distinguish between 'absolute power' (qudra muṭlaqa) and the implied second type. The text describes absolute power as the minimum by which the commanded act can be performed and a condition for every command.
The second type (not fully detailed) likely refers to a more complete or specific power, but the focus here is on the absolute.
5
State the legal effect (athar)
Conclude that when absolute power is present, the obligation stands; when absent, the obligation is either waived or a substitute is offered (e.g., tayammum for wudu).
This is the core of the Hanafi principle of taklīf bi al-muqaddarāt.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
پھر اس قدرت سے وہ قدرت حقیقت مراد نہیں جس کے ساتھ فعل ہوتا ہے کیونکہ وہ قدرت فعل سے پہلے نہیں ہوتی۔ لہذاوہ مکلف بنانے کا مدار نہیں بن سکتی بلکہ اس قدرت سے مراد وہ قدرت ہے جو اسباب اور آلات کی سلامتی اور اعضاء کے بیج ہونے کے معنی میں ہے کیونکہ یہ قدرت فعل سے پہلے ہوتی ہے لنداء ملک بنانے کا مدار ہوسکتی ہے تو اس بنا پر کہتے ہیں کہ دنسو کر نے کی قدرت اس وقت ہوگی جس وقت پانی ہوگا ورنہ تیم کریں گے۔ اور زکوۃ کی قدرت اس وقت ہوگی جب نصاب کا مالک ہوگا ورنہ زکوۃ معاف ہوگی پھر اس قدرت کی دو قسمیں ہیں۔ قوله وهى نوعان مطلق وهو ادنى ما يتمكن به المامو رين من أداء ما لزمه وهو شرط هى اداء كل امر والشرط تو همه لا حقيقته .
قدرت کی قسم اول قدرت ممکنہ :
(۱) پہلی سے مطلق قدرت اور یہ اس ادنیٰ قدرت کا نام ہے جس کی وجہ سے مکلف مامور بہ کے ادا کرنے پر قادر ہوتا ہے اور یہ ہر امر کے ادا کرنے کیلئے شرط ہے اور اس کی اتنی ہی مقدار شرط ہے کہ جس میں مامور بہ کو ادا کر سکے۔ نک مصنف نے قسم اور قسم میں فرق کرنے کیلئے قسم میں اونی کی قید بڑھادی ہے کیونکہ
Then by this power is not meant the power with which the act occurs, because that power does not exist before the act. Therefore it cannot be the basis for making someone obligated (mukallaf). Rather, by this power is meant the power which is in the sense of the safety of means and instruments and the soundness of limbs, because this power exists before the act and can be the basis for making someone obligated. Thus on this basis they say: the power to perform wudu will be when there is water, otherwise they will perform tayammum. And the power for zakah will be when one owns the nisab, otherwise zakah is waived. Then this power has two types. He said: 'They are two types: absolute (muṭlaq), which is the minimum by which the obligated person can perform what is required of him, and it is a condition for the performance of every command; and the condition is not its reality.'
The first type of power: absolute power (qudra mumkina):
(1) The first is absolute power, and it is the name for the minimal power by which the obligated person is able to perform the commanded act, and it is a condition for the performance of every command, and its quantity is only that by which he can perform the commanded act. Note: The author added the restriction of 'absolute' to distinguish between the two types.
Source pages p. 99

Commentary
This passage delves into the concept of qudra (power/ability) as a condition for taklīf (obligation). The text clarifies that the power meant here is not the power concurrent with the act (which comes after intention and effort), but rather the preconditions that make the act possible—availability of means (e.g., water for wudu, wealth for zakah) and physical ability (sound limbs). This is in line with the Hanafi usul principle that obligation depends on the possibility of performance; one cannot be obliged to do something impossible. The text then divides power into two types: the first is 'absolute power' (qudra muṭlaqa) which is the minimal ability to perform the act. This is the condition for every command (amr). The second type (implied but not detailed here) would be a more specific or complete ability. The commentator notes that the author clarified 'absolute' to differentiate it from the other type. This discussion is fundamental to understanding how Hanafi scholars determine the scope of obligations—what is within a person's capacity to do, considering external factors and physical ability.

Key Terms
قدرت مطلق (qudrah muṭlaqah): The minimal power or ability that enables the mukallaf to perform the commanded act; a condition for every command.
قدرت ممکنہ (qudrah mumkinah): Another term for 'absolute power' (qudrah muṭlaqah), emphasizing its minimal and possible nature.
شرط (sharṭ): A condition that must be present for the commanded act to be obligatory; in this case, the condition of power (qudrah).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the correct definition of qudra that serves as a condition for obligation?
A) The power that exists during the performance of the commanded act
B) The power that results from the act itself
C) The power that comes from the safety of means and instruments and the soundness of limbs before the act
D) The power that is created by intention

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, the condition for obligation is pre-existing power (qudra muṭlaqa), defined as the minimal capacity to perform the commanded act through available means and physical ability.

Possible Capacity as a Condition for Immediate Performance
Defining qudrat mumkin and its condition for ada' obligation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi usul concept of qudrat mumkin to determine when immediate performance (ada') is obligatory and distinguish it from the condition for makeup (qada').

Core Idea
Only the possibility of capacity, not its actual existence, is required for the obligation of immediate performance.

In Hanafi usul, the concept of qudrat mumkin (possible capacity) is crucial for understanding when a person becomes obliged to perform an act immediately. This lesson explores its definition, its scope, and its application to cases at the end of time, such as a convert embracing Islam just before sunset. We will see why mere possibility of sufficient time suffices, drawing on the extraordinary precedent of the sun stopping for prophets.

Guided Path
1
Identify the rule
Understand that qudrat mumkin is a condition (shart) only for the obligation of immediate performance (ada'), not for makeup (qada') except when qada' is itself immediate.
This is the foundational distinction.
2
Distinguish ada' and qada' applicability
Recognize that the condition applies to qada' only if the required act is due immediately; otherwise, it is a bequest or sin.
The text explicitly states this exception.
3
Understanding the condition: possibility vs actuality
Grasp that only the possibility (imkan) of having sufficient time is required, not the actual existence of that time.
This is the core of the principle.
4
Apply to the examples
Consider the cases of a child reaching puberty, a disbeliever converting, or a menstruating woman becoming pure at the very end of the prayer time; they become obliged even if only enough time for the opening takbir remains.
See how the principle works in concrete scenarios.
5
Connect to the naqli evidence
The miracle of the sun stopping for prophets (e.g., Sulayman) shows that Allah can extend time, making the possibility of sufficient time a valid basis for obligation.
This reinforces that possibility is sufficient.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
العبدت اور ادنی کی قید کی وجہ سے انقسام الشئی الی نفسہ والا اعتراض بھی نہیں کیا سکتا ۔ پھر یہ قدرت ممکن صرف ادا کیلئے شرط ہے قضا کیلئے مطلقا شرط نہیں ہے بلکہ قضاء کیلئے صرف اسوقت شرط ہوگی جب مطلوب فعل کی ادائیگی ہو ورنہ پھر وصیت ہوگی یا عدم ایصاء کی وجہ سے گناہ ہو گا۔ مزید یہ کہ پھر اس قدرت کا صرف امکان شرط ہے حقیقتاً اس کا پایا جانا شرط نہیں ۔ قوله حتى إذا بلغ الصبي أو أسلم الكافر أو طهرت الحائض في آخر الوقت لزمته الصلوة لتوهم الامتداد في آخر الوقت مقسم من قدرت کی تعریف ما يتمكن بها العبد ہے اور تم اون ما يتمكن بها بوقوف الشمس . تشریح...... مثلاً ظہر کی چار رکعت کیلئے یہ ضروری نہیں کہ اتنا وقت حقیقتاً پایا جائے جس میں چار رکعت پڑھی جاسکیں بلکہ صرف اس امر کا امکان کافی ہے کہ ہو سکتا ہے کہ وقت اللہ تعالیٰ کی طرف سے طویل ہو جائے۔ لہذا اگر بالکل آخری وقت میں میسی بالغ ہو گیا یا کا فرمسلمان ہو گیا یا حائضہ دم تیش سے پاک ہوگئی تو ان پر نماز ظہر ا ا زم ہو جائیگی اگر چہ صرف اتنا وقت باقی ہو جس میں محض کبیر تحریمہ ہی کہی جائے کیونکہ سورج کی رفتار رک جانے سے وقت کے لمبا ہونے کا احتمال ہے جس میں یہ افراد نماز ظہر ادا کر سکیں جیسا کہ حضرت سلیمان علیہ السلام اور حضرت یوشع بن نون علیہ السلام اور حضرت علی المرتضی رضی اللہ عنہ کیلئے وقت ایسا ہو گیا تھا حضرت سلیمان والی روایت دیگر دونوں روایات کے مقابلے میں قومی ہے۔ اور تفاسیر میں بھی مذکور تے لیکن دوسری دونوں روایات ضعیف ہیں ۔
Due to the restriction of worship and a lower cause, the objection that a thing is divided into itself cannot be raised. Then this possible power is a condition only for immediate performance, not absolutely for makeup, but for makeup it will be a condition only when the required act is performed, otherwise it will be a bequest or sin due to non-fulfillment. Moreover, only the possibility of this power is a condition, not its actual existence. His saying: 'Until when a child reaches puberty, or a disbeliever converts, or a menstruating woman becomes pure at the end of the time, the prayer becomes incumbent upon them due to the notion of extension at the end of the time.' Part of the definition of power is 'what the servant is capable of', and you have 'what he is capable of' by the stopping of the sun. Explanation: For example, for the four rak'ah of Zuhr it is not necessary that such time actually exists in which four rak'ah can be performed, but only the possibility that it could be that the time is lengthened by Allah is sufficient. Therefore, if at the very end of time a boy reaches puberty, or a disbeliever converts, or a menstruating woman becomes pure from blood, then Zuhr prayer becomes obligatory upon them, even if only enough time remains for just the Takbir Tahrima, because due to the stopping of the sun's motion there is a possibility of time lengthening, in which these individuals could perform the Zuhr prayer, just as time became like that for Prophet Sulayman (peace be upon him), Prophet Yusha' bin Nun (peace be upon him), and Ali al-Murtada (may Allah be pleased with him). The narration regarding Sulayman is strong compared to the other two narrations, and is also mentioned in exegeses, but the other two narrations are weak.
Source pages p. 100

Commentary
This passage discusses the first type of capacity (qudrat). The author refutes an objection about dividing a thing into itself by noting that the restriction of worship and a lower cause prevents it. He states that 'possible capacity' is required only for the immediate performance (ada') of an obligation, not for the makeup (qada') unless the makeup act is due immediately. Importantly, only the possibility of this capacity is needed, not its actual existence. He then quotes a text (likely from the matn) that gives examples: if a child reaches puberty, a disbeliever accepts Islam, or a menstruating woman becomes clean at the very end of the prayer time, they become obliged to pray even if only enough time remains for the opening takbir. This is because the sun stopping (as occurred for some prophets) raises the possibility of time extension. The author notes the strongest narration is about Prophet Sulayman. This illustrates that the mere possibility (imkan) of sufficient time is enough for the obligation of immediate performance.

Key Terms
قدرت ممکن (qudrat mumkin): The capacity that is merely possible to have; it is only a condition for the obligation of immediate performance, not for makeup, and only its possibility matters, not its actuality.

A) That actual time for the full prayer must exist.
B) That only the possibility of time extension is sufficient.
C) That he must have physical ability to perform all rak'at.
D) That he must have previously known the obligation.

Key Takeaway
Possible capacity (qudrat mumkin) is a condition only for immediate performance, and its mere possibility suffices, as exemplified by the sun stopping for prophets.

Perfect Capacity (Qudrat Kamilah) and Its Effect on Obligations
Defining qudrat kamilah and its effect on continuation of obligation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define qudrat kamilah, explain its effect on the continuity of an obligation, and apply the rule to examples such as zakat, 'ushr, and kharaj.

Core Idea
If facilitating capacity is lost, the obligation drops — continuity of ease is a condition for continuity of duty.

This lesson focuses on the second type of capacity in Hanafi usul: qudrat kamilah (perfect/facilitating capacity). Unlike mere possible capacity, this capacity must persist for the obligation to remain binding. We will explore how this rule explains the remission of zakat, 'ushr, and kharaj when wealth or produce is destroyed.

Guided Path
1
Define the term
Identify qudrat kamilah/muyassira and its distinguishing feature: it makes performance easy.
Contrast with qudrat mumkinah (possible capacity).
2
State the rule
The continuity of this capacity is a condition for the continuity of the obligation.
If the facilitating capacity ceases, the obligation drops entirely or partially.
3
Examine the examples
For zakat, 'ushr, and kharaj, note the conditions that indicate facilitating capacity (nisab, nine-tenths of produce left, ability to cultivate).
These conditions show that the capacity is not mere ownership but actual ease.
4
Apply the rule to partial vs. total loss
If the entire wealth/produce is destroyed, the obligation drops completely; if only part is destroyed, the obligation remains on the remaining portion proportionally.
The capacity is lost only to the extent of the destroyed portion.
5
Contrast with possible capacity
Understand that possible capacity alone does not sustain the obligation; the extra conditions signal that the capacity is facilitating.
This distinction is unique to Hanafi usul and explains many conditional obligations.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : وكامل وهو القدرة الميسرة للاداء ودوام هذه القدرة شرط لدوام الواجب . قدرت کی دوسری قسم قدرت کاملہ : قدرت کی دوسری قسم قدرت کاملہ ہے اور اس کو قدرت میسرہ بھی کہتے ہیں کیونکہ اس کی وجہ سے مامور بہ کا ادا کرنا آسان ہو جاتا ہے۔ اور میسرہ مشتق ہے یسر ( آسانی ) سے اور واجب کے دوام کیلئے اس قدرت کا دوام شرط ہے اگر یہ قدرت نہ پائی گئی تو واجب بھی نہیں رہے گا۔ قوله حتى تبطل الزكوة والعشر والخراج بهلاك المال چونکہ دوام قدرت شرط ہے اس لئے اگر مال ہلاک ہو جائے تو زکوة عشر اور خراج معاف ہو جاتے ہیں کیونکہ زکوۃ پر اصل قدرت تو صرف مال کا مالک بننے سے حاصل ہو جاتی ہے لیکن جب اس میں نصاب اور حولان حول کی شرط لگائی گئی تو معلوم ہوا کہ اس میں قدرت میسرہ ہے۔ لہذا اگر پورا نصاب ہلاک ہو گیا تو زکوۃ ساقط ہو جائیگی لیکن اگر بعض نصاب ہلاک ہو، باقی مال کی زکوۃ واجب رہے گی۔ اس لئے کہ ابتداء میں نصاب کی شرط صرف غنی مالداری" کے ثبوت کیلئے ہے تو جب غنی پائی گئی اس کے بعد بعض مال ہلاک ہو گیا تو باقی مال میں اس کے حصے کے مطابق میسر ( قدرت میسرہ ) باقی ہے۔ 1 ای طرح عشر میں قدرت ممکنہ صرف زراعت سے حاصل ہو جاتی ہے تو جب اس میں یہ شرط لگائی گئی کہ (نو) حصے زمین کی پیداوار کے مالک کے پاس رہیں گے تو معلوم ہوا کہ اس میں قدرت میسرہ ہے لہذا اگر کھیتی ہلاک ہوگئی تو عشر ساقط ہو جائیگا۔ اور اسی طرح خراج میں قدرت ممکنہ صرف زمین کے مالک ہونے سے حاصل ہو جاتی ہے لیکن جب اس میں یہ شرط لگائی گئی کہ زمین کا مالک اس زمین کی کاشت پر قادر ہو ، پانی بھی ہو کھیتی کے آلات بھی ہوں تو معلوم ہوا کہ اس میں قدرت میسرہ ہے لہذا اگر غلہ ہلاک ہو گیا تو خراج ساقط ہو جائے گا۔
His saying: 'And perfect, and it is the facilitating capacity for performance, and the continuity of this capacity is a condition for the continuity of the obligation.' The second type of capacity: perfect capacity. The second type of capacity is perfect capacity, and it is also called facilitating capacity because due to it the performance of what is commanded becomes easy. And 'muyassira' is derived from yusr (ease). For the continuity of the obligation, the continuity of this capacity is a condition; if this capacity is not found, then the obligation will not remain. His saying: 'Until zakat, 'ushr, and kharaj are nullified by the destruction of wealth.' Since the continuity of capacity is a condition, therefore if wealth is destroyed, zakat, 'ushr, and kharaj are remitted. Because original power for zakat is obtained only through owning wealth, but when the condition of nisab and passage of a year is imposed, it becomes clear that it involves facilitating capacity. So if the entire nisab is destroyed, zakat drops, but if part of the nisab is destroyed, zakat remains on the remaining wealth. Because initially the condition of nisab is only for establishing sufficiency, so when sufficiency is attained, after that if some wealth is destroyed, the facilitating capacity (qudrat muyassira) remains in the remaining wealth according to its share. Similarly, in 'ushr, possible capacity is obtained only through agriculture, so when the condition was imposed that nine portions of the land's produce remain with the owner, it became clear that it involves facilitating capacity. Therefore, if the crop is destroyed, 'ushr drops. And similarly, in kharaj, possible capacity is obtained only through being owner of the land, but when the condition was imposed that the landowner is capable of cultivating the land, has water, and agricultural tools, it became clear that it involves facilitating capacity. Therefore, if the grain is destroyed, kharaj drops.
Source pages p. 100

Commentary
This passage explains the second type of capacity: perfect or facilitating capacity (qudrat kamilah/muyassira). The author states that this capacity must persist for the obligation to continue; if it disappears, the obligation ceases. He illustrates with three examples: zakat, 'ushr (tithe on agricultural produce), and kharaj (land tax). In each case, the initial possible capacity (e.g., owning wealth, owning land) is not sufficient to sustain the obligation; instead, a facilitating capacity is required. For zakat, the additional conditions of nisab and passage of a year indicate that once sufficiency is established, the obligation remains only if the wealth persists; if the entire nisab is destroyed, zakat drops, but if only part is destroyed, zakat on the remaining amounts remains because the facilitating capacity still exists relative to the remaining wealth. For 'ushr, the condition that nine-tenths of the produce remains with the owner shows that the obligation depends on the actual availability of the produce; if the crop is destroyed, 'ushr drops. For kharaj, conditions like ability to cultivate, availability of water and tools show that the obligation only continues if the land is productive; if the grain is destroyed, kharaj drops. Thus, the continuity of perfect/facilitating capacity is necessary for the continuity of the obligation.

Key Terms
قدرت کاملہ (qudrat kamilah): Perfect capacity, also called facilitating capacity (muyassira), is the capacity that makes performance easy; its continuity is a condition for the obligation to remain in effect.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, if a person's entire nisab (minimum wealth for zakat) is destroyed after the passage of one year, what happens to the zakat obligation?
A) Zakat must still be paid from any remaining wealth.
B) Zakat drops entirely because the facilitating capacity is lost.
C) Zakat remains but delayed.
D) Zakat becomes a debt on the person.

Key Takeaway
The continuity of qudrat kamilah (facilitating capacity) is a condition for the continuity of obligations dependent on ease of performance; if the capacity is completely lost, the obligation drops.
