Ikhtiyar in Shar'i Actions: Ability and Permission
Conceptual analysis of ikhtiyar and prohibition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two components of ikhtiyar in shar'i actions and explain why a definitive prohibition does not negate the servant's choice but removes legal permission.

Core Idea
Choice in shari'ah requires both ability and permission; prohibition withdraws permission, not ability.

This passage delves into the concept of ikhtiyar (choice) as it applies to acts governed by divine law. The author clarifies that true ikhtiyar is not merely physical capability but also requires authorization (idhn) from the Lawgiver. A key nuance emerges: when an act is prohibited, the servant still retains the physical ability to perform it, but the legal permission is removed—thus the act is not within the scope of ikhtiyar. The passage warns against the erroneous view that prohibition annihilates choice altogether, which would reduce prohibition to an impossible negation.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish physical ability from legal authorization
Identify that 'ability' (qudra) is the capacity to act, while 'authorization' (idhn) is the permission from the Lawgiver. Ikhtiyar in shar'i actions requires both.
Physical ability alone does not constitute lawful choice; e.g., one can physically steal but has no legal permission.
2
Understand the essence-attribute distinction
An act may be legislated (mashru') in its essence but prohibited in a particular attribute. For example, prayer is legislated, but praying at forbidden times is prohibited due to the attribute of timing.
This allows an act to be both permissible in principle and impermissible in a specific instance.
3
Analyze the claim that prohibition invalidates choice
If we assert that prohibition nullifies the servant's choice, then the prohibition would become a negation (nafy) of the act's very possibility. This is self-evidently invalid because prohibition does not make the act existentially impossible.
The author argues that such a view leads to absurdity; thus, prohibition does not eliminate choice but only removes legal permission.
4
Synthesize the correct position
Conclude that ikhtiyar is preserved when an act is prohibited: the servant still has the ability but lacks permission. Therefore, the prohibition is a legal bar, not an existential negation.
The servant is accountable because the act remains within his power; he chooses to disobey.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اور ہر چیز میں اسی طرح کا اختیار ہوتا ہے جو اس کے مناسب ہو۔ افعال شرعیہ میں اختیار یہ ہے کہ کسی کام کے کرنے پر قادر ہو اور اسے اس کے کرنے سے رہ جائے اور افعال شرعیہ میں اختیار یہ ہے کہ اس کو شارع کی جانب سے اختیار ہو گویا اس کام کی اجازت بھی ہوگی اور اس سے بھی [؟] ہوگی اور یہ دونوں باتیں اس وقت جمع ہو سکتی ہیں جب ہم یہ کہیں کہ یہ فعل اپنی اصل کے اعتبار سے مشروع ہے اور اپنے وصف کے اعتبار سے منہی عنہ ہے۔ لیکن اگر ہم یہ کہیں کہ افعال شرعیہ میں نہی ثابت ہوتا ہے تو اس طرح بندے کے اختیار کو باطل کرنا لازم آئے گا اور نہی نفی بن جائیگی جس کا بطلان محتاج دلیل نہیں۔
And in everything there is a similar kind of choice that is appropriate to it. In shar'i actions, choice is that one is able to do an action and refrains from doing it? And in shar'i actions, choice is that he has authorization from the Lawgiver, meaning there is permission for the action and also from it? And these two matters can be combined when we say that this action is legislated in its essence and prohibited in its attribute. But if we say that in shar'i actions prohibition is established, then it necessitates invalidating the servant's choice, and the prohibition becomes a negation, the invalidity of which does not need proof.
Source pages p. 119

Commentary
This passage discusses the concept of ikhtiyar (choice) in relation to shar'i actions. It distinguishes between physical ability (qudra) and legal authorization (idhn). In shar'i actions, ikhtiyar requires both capacity and permission from the Lawgiver. The author explains that two aspects can coexist: an act may be legislated in its essence (asl) but prohibited in its attribute (wasf). However, if a prohibition is firmly established, it negates the servant's choice, turning the prohibition into an absolute negation, which is self-evidently invalid. This is a typical Hanafi usul discussion about the interaction between command and prohibition.

Key Terms
اختیار (ikhtiyar): In shar'i actions, the combination of physical ability and legal permission or authorization from the Lawgiver.
نہی (nahi): A prohibition from the Lawgiver that, when established, negates the servant's choice by rendering the act impermissible.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) The act becomes obligatory.

Key Takeaway
Ikhtiyar in shar'i actions requires both physical ability and legal permission; a definitive prohibition removes permission but not ability, preserving the servant's accountability.

Ruling of Mushtarak: Tawaqquf and Tarjih
States the ruling for mushtarak and demonstrates tarjih with the example of 'quru'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle of tawaqquf and tarjih to determine the intended meaning of a mushtarak word in a legal text.

Core Idea
Mushtarak requires suspension of judgment until contextual analysis yields a preponderant meaning.

The Hanafi school holds that when a word has multiple possible meanings, one cannot simply pick any or accept all at once. Instead, the mujtahid must pause (tawaqquf) and carefully examine the context (siyaq wa sabaq) to determine which meaning is more likely. This lesson explains that principle and demonstrates it through the classical example of the word 'quru'.

Guided Path
1
Identify the mushtarak term
Find the word in the text that has more than one possible legal meaning. In the example, the word 'quru' is mushtarak between menstruation and purity.
2
List the possible meanings
State the known meanings based on language and prior usage. For 'quru', the two meanings are menstruation (days of blood) and purity (tahr).
3
Apply contextual and linguistic analysis
Examine the surrounding text (siyaq), subject matter, and purpose. Also analyze linguistic properties such as root, plural form, and semantic attributes. In the example, the word is triliteral, its plural minimum is three, and it implies gathering and transfer. Menstruation involves gathering and transfer of blood; purity does not.
The attribute of gathering and transfer is decisive.
4
Determine the preponderant meaning
Weigh the evidence and select the meaning that best fits the context and linguistic criteria. In the example, menstruation is preponderant because it aligns with gathering and transfer.
5
Formulate the ruling
Apply the chosen meaning to derive the legal ruling. For instance, in the context of 'iddah, the meaning of menstruation leads to the ruling that the waiting period is three menstrual cycles.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله وحكمه التوقف فيه بشرط التأمل ليترجح بعض و جوهه للعمل به
(۳) مشترک کا حکم مشترک کا حکم یہ ہے کہ اس کے متعدد معانی کوملحوظ رکھ کر مقام کی نسبت سے سیاق وسباق پر غور و فکر کے ذریعے سے اس کے کسی ایک معنی کو ترجیح دی جائیگی تا کہ اس پر عمل کیا جا سکے۔
مثال کے ذریعے وضاحت :
قردہ ایک لفظ مشترک ہے ہم نے اس لفظ میں کئی طریقوں سے غور و فکر کیا مثلاً
ہم نے دیکھا :
(1) اس لفظ کی صفت لفظ ثلاثہ ہے اور خاص ہے۔
(۲) دوسرا یہ ہے کہ اقل جمع تین ہے۔
(۳) تیسرا یہ ہے کہ جمع اور انتقال کے معنی میں ہے۔
اب اگر قروہ سے مرد دوم ( خون حیض) ہو تو ظاہر ہے کہ دم میں جمع اورمنتقل ہونے والی صفت پائی جاتی ہے۔
پس اگر اس سے مراد ایام دم ہوں تو ایام حیض اجتماع اور انتقال کا محل ہیں۔ بخلاف طہر کے کہ نہ وہ جمع ہونے والا ہے اور نہ منتقل ہونے والا اور نہ وہ جمع ہونے اور انتقال کا محل ہے۔
His statement: 'And its ruling is suspension (tawaqquf) in it, with the condition of contemplation, so that some of its aspects become preponderant to act upon.' (3) The ruling of mushtarak: The ruling of mushtarak is that, keeping in mind its multiple meanings, one should give preponderance to one of its meanings through contemplation of context (siyaq wa sabaq) in relation to the situation, so that it can be acted upon. Clarification through example: 'Quru' is a mushtarak word. We contemplate this word in several ways: (1) The word's property is that it is a triliteral word and specific. (2) Secondly, that the minimum of a plural is three. (3) Thirdly, that it has the meaning of gathering and transferring. Now if by 'quru' the second meaning (blood of menstruation) is intended, then clearly blood has the attribute of gathering and transferring. So if it means the days of blood, then the days of menstruation are the locus of aggregation and transfer. Unlike purity (tahr), which is neither something that gathers nor transfers, nor is it a locus for gathering and transfer.
Source pages p. 142

Commentary
This passage explains the ruling of a mushtarak word according to Hanafi usul. The principle is tawaqquf: one must suspend judgment when encountering a mushtarak term and cannot act until the intended meaning is determined through deliberation and contextual analysis. The author provides an example using the word 'quru', which is mushtarak between menstruation and purity. He outlines a method of tarjih (preponderance): by examining the word's intrinsic qualities (e.g., triliteral root, specific nature) and its linguistic implications (minimum of three, meanings of gathering and transfer). Since the meaning of menstruation (blood) involves gathering and transfer, and the days of menstruation are the locus of such events, whereas purity lacks these attributes, the preponderant meaning in contexts that involve gathering and transfer is menstruation. This reasoning shows how a mujtahid uses contextual clues (siyaq wa sabaq) and linguistic properties to choose one meaning over another, enabling legal action based on the preferred interpretation.

Key Terms
توقف (tawaqquf): Suspension of judgement; the act of pausing and not proceeding until the intended meaning of a mushtarak is determined through contemplation and contextual evidence.
ترجیح (tarjih): Giving preponderance to one meaning over others based on contextual clues and linguistic analysis.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Hanafi usul, what must be done when a mushtarak word appears in a text?
A) Accept all meanings simultaneously
B) Immediately act upon the most common meaning
C) Suspend judgment and seek preponderance through contemplation
D) Ignore the word as ambiguous

Key Takeaway
Hanafi usul mandates tawaqquf (suspension) for mushtarak words, requiring tarjih (preponderance) through contextual and linguistic analysis before deriving a ruling.

The Ruling of Muawwal (Interpreted Text)
Defines muawwal and explains its ruling and epistemological status.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define muawwal, state its legal ruling, identify its epistemological status as zanni, and explain the consequence for the denier according to Hanafi usul.

Core Idea
Acting on muawwal is wajib but probabilistic; rejecting it never reaches kufr.

This lesson introduces muawwal, a key category in Hanafi usul: a text whose apparent meaning is abandoned for a weaker interpretation due to a non-definitive evidence. We will examine its ruling, its epistemological status, and the important practical consequence that denying this meaning does not render one a disbeliever.

Guided Path
1
Understand the definition of muawwal
Muawwal is a text whose apparent (zahir) meaning is set aside for a weaker interpretation because of a dalil that is not strong enough to make the new meaning certain.
2
Identify the ruling (hukm) of muawwal
The ruling is wajib: it must be acted upon, but it is based on probability (zann), not certainty (qat').
3
Examine the proof (dalil) for this ruling
The author cites a hadith that the mujtahid may be correct or mistaken, but still receives reward. This shows ijtihad is probabilistic, so the interpreted meaning also carries probability.
4
Recognize the practical consequence (fai'da)
Because the meaning is zanni, the one who rejects it is not accused of kufr, as the true meaning might be the opposite.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : وحكمه العمل به على احتمال الغلط (۲) موول کا حکم اس پر [عمل؟] کرنا واجب ہے ظنی ہے چونکہ اس میں کسی معنی کی [؟؟] فعل مجتہد ہوتی ہے اور حدیث میں آتا ہے کہ مجتہد اپنے اجتہاد میں کبھی [پیدا؟] برحق ہوتا ہے اور کبھی غلطی و خطاء کا شکار ہو جاتا ہے تا ہم اسے اجر ضرور ملتا ہے۔ الغرض جب اس میں خطاء کا احتمال آگیا تو اس میں [ظنیت؟] آگئی اس میں ظنیت کا [فائدہ؟] یہ ہوگا کہ اس معنی مقولہ کے منکر کو کافر نہیں کہا جائے گا کیونکہ ممکن ہے کہ حق یہ معنی نہ ہو بلکہ اس کا جانب مقابل ہو ۔
His saying: Its ruling is to act upon it with the possibility of error. (2) The ruling of muawwal: Acting upon it is obligatory, it is zanni because in it, some meaning [??] by the action of the mujtahid, and it comes in hadith that the mujtahid sometimes attains the truth in his ijtihad and sometimes falls into error and mistake, yet he certainly receives reward. In short, when the possibility of error enters it, then [zann] enters it. The benefit of zann is that the denier of this interpreted meaning will not be called a disbeliever, because it is possible that the truth is not this meaning but rather its opposite.
Source pages p. 145

Commentary
This passage discusses the ruling of muawwal, which is a text that has been interpreted away from its apparent meaning due to a weak evidence (dalil). Its ruling is that acting upon this interpreted meaning is obligatory (wajib), but it is based on probability (zann), not certainty. The author supports this by citing a hadith that a mujtahid may be correct or mistaken but always receives reward. The key benefit (fai'da) of this zanni status is that rejecting this meaning does not constitute kufr, because the true meaning might be the opposite. This is a standard Hanafi usul principle: only clear, definitive texts (qat'i) can make rejection kufr.

Key Terms
موول (muawwal): A text whose apparent meaning has been abandoned for a weaker interpretation due to a dalil that is not strong enough to make the new meaning definitive.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling of acting upon muawwal according to the Hanafi school?
A) It is forbidden because it is not the apparent meaning.
B) It is obligatory (wajib) but based on probability (zann).
C) It is recommended but not obligatory.
D) It is obligatory with certainty (qat'i).

Key Takeaway
Muawwal is acted upon as a wajib ruling, but its probabilistic nature (zann) means that rejection of it does not constitute disbelief.

Definition of Haqiqah and Its Types
Defining haqiqah and its divisions based on the custom of coinage

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define haqiqah and distinguish its three types based on the custom of coinage (wad').

Core Idea
Haqiqah is a word used for its original coinage, whether linguistic, legal, or customary.

In Hanafi usul al-fiqh, understanding whether a word is used literally (haqiqah) or figuratively (majaz) is fundamental to correct interpretation of revealed texts. This passage from Khulasat al-Anwar defines haqiqah and explains the types of wad' that give rise to different categories of haqiqah. You will learn not only the definition but also the ruling (hukm) of haqiqah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definition of haqiqah
Locate the sentence defining haqiqah: 'حقيقة اسم لكل لفظ اريد به ما وضع له' – a word used for its original coinage.
2
Understand the meaning of wad'
Wad' is the assignment of a word to a meaning. The passage explains three possible assigners: language, Lawgiver, and custom.
3
Distinguish the three types of wad'
Linguistic (لغوي), legal (شرعي), customary (عرفي) – further divided into specific (خاص) and general (عام). Memorize the examples: 'insan', 'salah', 'fi'l', 'dabbah'.
4
Apply the ruling of haqiqah
The ruling (hukm) is that the meaning for which the word was coined is actually intended and exists in the context.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أما الحقيقة فاسم لكل لفظ اريد به ما وضع له وحكمها وجود ما وضع له خاصاً كان أو عاماً. تقسیم ثانی سے فارغ ہونے کے بعد اب مصنف رحمہ اللہ تقسیم ثالث کو شروع فرماتے ہیں اور وہ ہے حقیقت اور مجاز صریح اور کنایہ۔ حقیقت کی تعریف : حقیقت اس لفظ کا نام ہے جس سے وہ معنی مراد ہو جس کیلئے اس کو وضع کیا گیا ہو۔ وضع کی تعریف اب وضع کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ اس لفظ کو کسی معنی کیلئے متعین کرنا پھر معین کرنا اگر واضع لغت کی طرف سے ہو تو وہ ضع لغوی ہوگی جیسے انسان کی وضع حیوان ناطق کیلئے۔ اور اگر شارع کی طرف سے ہو تو وضع شرعی ہوگی جیسے صلوٰۃ کی وضع نماز کیلئے ۔ اور اگر یہ تعین کسی قوم مخصوص کی طرف سے ہو تو وضع عرفی خاص ہوگی جیسے فعل کی وضع کلمہ مخصوص کیلئے ۔ اور اگر تعیین عوام " عرف عام کی طرف سے ہو تو وضع عرفی عام ہوگی اس کی مثال دابتہ ہے جس کو چوپائے کیلئے وضع کیا گیا ہے۔ حقیقت کا حکم : ہو یا عام۔ حقیقت کا حکم یہ ہیکہ جس معنی کیلئے اس کو وضع کیا گیا ہے وہ پایا جائے خواہ وہ معنی خاص قوله : وأما المجاز فاسم لما اريد به غير ما وضع له لمنا سبة بينها وحكمه وجود ما استعير له خاصاً كان أو عام.
As for haqiqah, it is a name for every word that is used for what it was coined for, and its ruling is that the meaning for which it was coined exists, whether specific or general. After finishing the second division, the author (may Allah have mercy on him) begins the third division, which is haqiqah and majaz, and sarih and kinayah. Definition of haqiqah: Haqiqah is the name of a word from which the meaning for which it was coined is intended. Definition of wad': The meaning of wad' is to assign a word to a meaning. If the assigner is from the language, it is linguistic wad', like the coining of 'insan' for 'hayawan natiq'. If it is from the Lawgiver, it is legal wad', like the coining of 'salah' for prayer. If the assignment is from a particular group, it is specific customary wad', like the coining of 'fi'l' for a specific word. If the assignment is from the general public, it is general customary wad', like the example of 'dabbah' which was coined for quadrupeds. The ruling of haqiqah is that the meaning for which it was coined is found, whether that meaning is specific. He said: 'As for majaz, it is a name for what is used for other than what it was coined for, due to a relationship between them, and its ruling is that the meaning for which it was borrowed exists, whether specific or general.'
Source pages p. 158

Commentary
This passage introduces the crucial usul distinction between haqiqah (literal) and majaz (figurative). It first defines haqiqah as a word used for its original coinage, then explains the three types of coinage: linguistic (by language), legal (by the Lawgiver), and customary (by a specific group or the general public). The ruling of haqiqah is that the original meaning is actually intended. The passage then begins the definition of majaz as using a word for a meaning other than its original, based on a relationship, and its ruling is that the borrowed meaning is intended. This lays the foundation for understanding textual interpretation in Hanafi usul, particularly in distinguishing apparent meanings from metaphorical ones.

Key Terms
حقیقت (haqiqah): A word used for its original coinage.
مجاز (majaz): A word used for a meaning other than its original due to a relationship.
وضع (wad'): The assignment of a word to a meaning.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling (hukm) of haqiqah?
A) That the word is used metaphorically.
B) That the meaning for which it was coined exists.
C) That the word is ambiguous.
D) That the word is used for a non-original meaning.

Key Takeaway
Haqiqah is a word used for its original coinage, and its ruling is that the original meaning is present—whether linguistic, legal, or customary.

The Particle 'بل': Definition and Legal Implications
Definition of 'بل' as a particle of abandonment and establishment

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule for the particle 'بل' to distinguish between its effect in performative utterances (insha') and reports (akhbar).

Core Idea
بل annuls the prior in reports but not in performatives; in divorce, the first divorce remains effective.

This lesson examines the Arabic particle 'بل' (rather) and its legal implications in Hanafi usul. The key is to understand that the effect of 'بل' depends on whether the statement is a performative (insha') like divorce, or a report (akhbar) like an acknowledgment. We will see why saying 'one divorce, rather two' results in three, while saying 'one thousand, rather two' results in two thousand owed.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definition of 'بل'
The passage defines 'بل' as a particle that establishes what follows and turns away from what precedes, as a correction (tadaruk). Note the key phrase: على سبيل التدارك.
2
Distinguish between insha' and akhbar
Understand that the effect of turning away (الاعراض) applies only in reports (akhbar), not in performatives (insha'). In insha', the prior utterance has legal effect and cannot be retroactively annulled.
insha' includes divorce, marriage, etc.; akhbar includes acknowledgments and news.
3
Apply to the divorce example
The husband says 'one divorce, rather two'. Since divorce is insha', the first divorce is effective immediately. 'بل' does not annul it; it adds another, resulting in three divorces total (1 + 2).
Text: 'فتطلق ثلاثاً'
4
Apply to the acknowledgment example
If someone says 'I owe him one thousand, rather two thousand', this is a report (akhbar). 'بل' annuls the first, so only the second is established. The debt is two thousand.
Text: 'فإذا قال له علي ألف بل ألفان لزمه ألفان'
5
Summarize the rule
بل annuls the prior in akhbar but adds without annulling in insha'. The key factor is whether the prior utterance created a legal effect.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : وبل لا ثبات ما بعده والاعراض عما قبله على سبيل التدارك فتطلق ثلاثاً اذا قال لامرأته المؤطوء أنت طالق واحدة بل ثنتين لأنه لم يملك ابطال الأول فيقعان بخلاف قوله له على الف بل الفان - بل : بل اپنے مالعبد کے اثبات کیلئے اور اپنے ماقبل سے اعراض کیلئے آتا ہے تدارک کے طریقے پر یعنی اس امر کا اظہار کرنے کیلئے کہ بل کے ماقبل کے تکلم میں غلطی ہوگئی اس لئے کہ وہ مقصود نہیں تھا بلکہ متصور اس کا ما بعد تھا جیسے جا ، نی زید بل عمر و سر و کیلئے تو مجنیت ثابت ہو جائیگی اور زید میں دو احتمال ہیں لیکن اگر جملہ منفیہ ہو یعنی ما جاء في زيد بل عمروتو اس صورت میں بعض لوگ کہتے ہیں کہ عمرو کی طرف نفی اور بعض کہتے ہیں کہ عمرو کی طرف اثبات متو جہ ہو گا ۔ تفريح ..... اگر کسی نے اپنی مدخولہ بیوی سے کہا انت طالق واحدة بل شنتين تو تین طلاقیں واقع ہو جائینگی۔ اس لئے کہ اخبار میں تو ماقبل سے اعراض کیا جاسکتا ہے لیکن ان اعراض جا سکتا لیکن اگر کسی نے کہا لہ علی الف بل الفان کہا تو صرف دو ہزار لازم ہو نگے کیونکہ یہ اقرار اور اخبار ہے لہذا اس میں ماقبل سے اعراض ہوسکتا ہے
قوله : وبل لاثبات ما بعده والاعراض عما قبله على سبيل التدارك فتطلق ثلاثاً اذا قال لامرأته المؤطوء أنت طالق واحدة بل ثنتين لأنه لم يملك ابطال الأول فيقعان بخلاف قوله له على الف بل الفان - بل: 'بل' is used for establishing what comes after it and for turning away from what comes before it in the manner of correction (tadaruk), i.e., to express that there was an error in the speech before 'بل' because it was not intended, rather what was intended is what comes after. For example, 'جاءني زيد بل عمرو' so 'عمرو' is established, and for 'زيد' there are two possibilities. But if the sentence is negative, i.e., 'ما جاءني زيد بل عمرو', then in that case some say that the negation applies to 'عمرو' and some say that affirmation applies to 'عمرو'. Example: if someone says to his wife whom he has consummated the marriage with: 'أنت طالق واحدة بل ثنتين', then three divorces occur because he does not have the power to annul the first, so both fall. Unlike if he says 'له علي ألف بل ألفان' then only two thousand are owed because it is an acknowledgment (iqrar) and a report (khabar), so he can turn away from what precedes.
Source pages p. 188

Commentary
This passage defines the particle 'بل' and its effect on legal statements. The key distinction is between performative utterances (insha') like divorce, where the prior effect cannot be undone, and reports (akhbar) like acknowledgments, where the speaker can correct himself. In the divorce example, saying 'one divorce, rather two' results in three divorces because the first is not voided. In the acknowledgment example, saying 'one thousand, rather two thousand' results in only two thousand being owed because the first is considered an error.

Key Terms
بل (bal): Particle meaning 'rather', used for correction, annuls previous and establishes next
تدارك (tadaruk): Correction, fixing an error in speech

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a man says to his consummated wife 'أنت طالق واحدة بل ثنتين', how many divorces occur?
A) One
B) Two
C) Three
D) None

Key Takeaway
The particle 'بل' annuls the prior in reports (akhbar) but not in performatives (insha'), so in divorce the divorces accumulate.

8 min
The Particle 'لكن' and Its Legal Functions
Definition of 'لكن' as a particle of istidrak after negation with conditions for 'atf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the conditions under which 'لكن' functions as a coordinating conjunction ('atf) versus an independent sentence (isti'naf) in legal texts, and apply these conditions to analyze example cases.

Core Idea
'لكن' coordinates only when negation and affirmation pertain to different things in connected speech; otherwise it starts a new sentence.

In Hanafi usul al-fiqh, particles like 'لكن' (but) carry specific legal implications. This lesson unpacks its dual function: as a coordinating conjunction that links two statements, or as an indicator of a new, independent sentence that cancels a previous legal statement. Understanding this distinction is crucial for interpreting contracts, oaths, and legal rulings where a speaker uses 'لكن' after a negation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the particle and its form
First, locate 'لكن' in the text and determine whether it is light (mukhaffafah) or heavy (mushaddadah). The light form is the coordinating conjunction; the heavy form resembles a verb but still indicates istidrak.
In legal texts, both forms appear, but the conditions for 'atf apply only to the light form.
2
Check connectedness of speech
Examine whether the clause before and after 'لكن' are directly connected (mutasil). If the speech is continuous and the second part immediately follows the first without interruption, it meets the first condition for 'atf.
If the speech is interrupted or begins a new topic, 'لكن' likely starts a new sentence.
3
Analyze negation and affirmation
Determine what is being negated in the first part and what is being affirmed in the second. The negation must be of one thing (e.g., an act or quality) and the affirmation of a different thing. If they are the same, 'لكن' cannot coordinate.
This is the key condition that distinguishes 'atf from isti'naf.
4
Apply the conditions to the example
In the slave girl marriage case, the master says 'I do not permit the marriage, but I permit it for 150 dirhams.' Since the negation and affirmation are about the same act (the marriage), the conditions are not met, so 'لكن' is isti'naf, meaning the first marriage is cancelled and a new one is formed.
If the master had said 'I do not permit it for 100, but I permit it for 150', the negation is about the dower amount, not the marriage itself, so 'لكن' coordinates and the original marriage remains.
5
Derive the legal consequence
Based on whether 'لكن' is 'atf or isti'naf, determine the legal effect. For 'atf, the initial statement stands with an exception or addition. For isti'naf, the initial statement is overridden and a new ruling applies.
This derivation is critical in fiqh for contracts, oaths, and judicial decisions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : ولكن للاستدراك، بعد النفى غير أن العطف عند اتساق الكلام والا فهو مستأنف كالأمة اذا تزوجت بغیر اذن مولاها بمائة درهم فقال لا اجيز النكاح ولكن اجيزه بمائة وخمسين در هما ان هذا فسخ للنكاح وجعل لكن مبتد أ لأن هذا فى فعل واثباته بعينه . لكن : لكن نفی کے بعد استدراک کیلئے آتا ہے یعنی سابق سے جو و ہم پیدا ہوا ہو اس کو دور کر نے کیلئے آتا ہے جیسے قول ما جاء فى زيد لكن عمر وا پھر اگر یہ مخففہ ہو تو عاطفہ ہوگا اور اگر مشدودہ ہو تو حروف مشبہ با فعل میں سے ہوگا۔ لیکن یہ عطف اس وقت صحیح ہو گا جب کہ کلام مرتب ہو یعنی سابق کلام کیساتھ متصل ہو اور نفی ایک چیز کی ہو اور اثبات اس کے علاوہ دوسری چیز کا ہو۔ اگر ان دونوں شرطوں میں سے ایک شرط بھی نہ پائی گئی تو کلام مستانفہ ہو گا معطوفہ نہیں ہوگا مثلاً اگر کسی لونڈی نے اپنے مولی کی اجازت کے بغیہ سود در هم پر نکاح کر لیا اور موٹی نے کيا لا اجيز النكاح ولكن اجيزه بمائة وخمسین درهما ) تو یہ نکاح کو فسخ کرنا ہوگا (لكن)) متانفہ ہوگا کیونکہ یہ بعینہ ایک ہی فعل کی نفی اور اس کا اثبات ہے تو اول کلام آخر کلام سے متناقض ہو جائیگا لہذا ہم یوں سمجھیں گے کہ مولی نے پہلے نکاح کو فسخ کر دیا اور پھرنے مہر پر دوسرا نکاح کیا لیکن اگر مولی نے اسکے جواب میں کہا ( لا اجيز النكاح بمائة ولكن اجيزه بمائة و خمسين در هما) تو اصل نکاح باقی رہے گا اور نفی صرف مائتہ کی قید کی ہو گی ۔
قوله : ولكن للاستدراك، بعد النفى غير أن العطف عند اتساق الكلام والا فهو مستأنف كالأمة اذا تزوجت بغیر اذن مولاها بمائة درهم فقال لا اجيز النكاح ولكن اجيزه بمائة وخمسين در هما ان هذا فسخ للنكاح وجعل لكن مبتد أ لأن هذا فى فعل واثباته بعينه. لكن: 'لكن' comes after negation for istidrak (rectification), i.e., to remove any doubt that arose from the preceding. For example, 'ما جاءني زيد لكن عمرو'. Then if it is light (mukhaffafah) it is a coordinating conjunction, and if it is heavy (mushaddadah) it is among the letters resembling verbs. But this 'atf is correct only when the speech is connected (mutasil) and the negation is of one thing and the affirmation of a different thing. If one of these two conditions is missing, then the speech is isti'naf (new sentence), not 'atf. For example, if a slave girl marries for one hundred dirhams without her master's permission, and the master says, 'I do not permit the marriage, but I permit it for one hundred and fifty dirhams,' then this is a cancellation (faskh) of the marriage, and 'لكن' is isti'naf because it is the negation and affirmation of the same act. So we understand that the master first cancelled the marriage and then performed a new marriage for the new dower. But if the master said, 'I do not permit the marriage for one hundred, but I permit it for one hundred and fifty dirhams,' then the original marriage remains, and the negation is only of the condition of one hundred.
Source pages p. 189

Commentary
This passage defines the particle 'لكن' and its usage in legal contexts. It distinguishes between 'atf (coordination) and isti'naf (new sentence) based on conditions of connectedness and differences in the subjects of negation and affirmation. The example of the slave girl's marriage illustrates: if the master negates and affirms the same act, 'لكن' is isti'naf, meaning the first act is cancelled and a new one performed. If the negation and affirmation are of different aspects (like the dower amount), 'لكن' can coordinate and the original marriage remains valid.

Key Terms
لكن (lākin): Particle meaning 'but', used after negation for rectification
استدراك (istidrāk): Rectification, removal of a misunderstanding or doubt
مستأنف (musta'naf): A new sentence not grammatically dependent on the previous

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When does 'لكن' function as a coordinating conjunction ('atf)?
A) When it is light (mukhaffafah) and the speech is connected with negation of one thing and affirmation of another
B) When it is heavy (mushaddadah)
C) Always
D) Never

Key Takeaway
The particle 'لكن' coordinates only when speech is connected and the negation and affirmation refer to different matters; otherwise it begins a new sentence with legal consequences.

intermediate
6 min
Interpreting the Ba' in Tayammum: Literal Meaning vs. Legal Context
Responding to an objection about the meaning of ba' in tayammum verse

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle of istihsan to resolve apparent contradictions between a text's literal meaning and its intended legal ruling.

Core Idea
Tayammum is the deputy of wudu: the ruling follows the original, not the literal particle.

This passage presents a classic hermeneutical challenge: the letter ba' in the tayammum verse appears to imply partial wiping, yet the legal ruling requires full coverage. The Hanafi response, grounded in the concept of substitution (khalafiyya), demonstrates how usul al-fiqh principles like istihsan can override literal meanings when the legal context demands it. Let's analyse this objection and its rebuttal step by step.

Guided Path
1
Identify the linguistic feature
Locate the particle ba' in the tayammum verse. Note its literal meaning in Arabic: it can indicate partiality (tab'id) or attachment (ilsaq).
The objector relies on the literal meaning of partiality.
2
State the objection
Understand that the objector argues that because ba' enters upon 'face' and 'hands', it implies wiping only part of them, not the entire surface.
3
Identify the intended ruling
Recognize that the desired legal effect is full coverage, as in wudu. Why would the Shari'ah require full coverage? Because tayammum is a substitute for wudu.
4
Locate the Hanafi response
The response states that tayammum is a deputy (khalifah) of wudu, so the ruling of the original (full coverage) applies to the substitute.
This is an application of qiyas and istihsan.
5
Evaluate the role of istihsan
Ask: Why is the literal meaning overridden? Because the context (siyaq) and the purpose (maqsad) of the law indicate that the substitute must mirror the original in its essential ruling.
Istihsan allows departure from literal analogy when a stronger evidence (here, the principle of substitution) demands it.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اللہ علیہ وسلم کا عمل کہ آپ نے مقدار ناصیہ پرسح کیا وہ اس کا بیان ہے۔
اعتراض ... اگر کوئی اعتراض کرے کہ تیم میں وجہ اور ید دونوں پر باء داخل ہے حالانکہ اس کا استیعاب مراد ہے۔
جواب چونکہ تیم وضو کا خلیفہ ہے لہذا اس کیساتھ اصل والا معاملہ کیا جائیگا۔
The action of the Prophet (peace be upon him) that he wiped over the amount of the forelock is an explanation of that. Objection: If someone objects that in tayammum, the letter ba' enters upon both the face and the hands, although its intended meaning is covering completely. Response: Since tayammum is the deputy of wudu, therefore the same treatment as the original will be given to it.
Source pages p. 200

Commentary
This passage is a textual analysis of the particle ba' (باء) as used in the verse of tayammum. An objector argues that ba' normally indicates partiality (تبعيض), but the intended meaning in the verse is complete coverage (استيعاب) of the face and hands. The response resolves this by noting that tayammum is a substitute (خليفة) for wudu. In wudu, the command to wash the face implies full coverage; by analogy, the deputy ruling follows the original. Thus, despite the literal implication of ba', the legal effect is full coverage because of the nature of substitution. This is a classic Hanafi use of qiyas and istihsan based on the relationship between an act and its substitute.

Key Terms
باء (ba'): A particle that can indicate attachment or partiality; here specifically in the context of tayammum, the objection is that it implies partial wiping but the intended meaning is full coverage.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) Because tayammum is a substitute for wudu, and the original requires full coverage
C) Because ba' in the Quran always means full coverage
D) Because the objector is mistaken about the meaning of ba'

Key Takeaway
The literal meaning of a particle may be overridden by the legal context of substitution (khalafiyya) through the principle of istihsan.

The Hanafi Principle of Ghayah with 'Ila'
Analysis of 'ila' as a ghayah limit

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi usul principle of ghayah to determine whether a limit (ghayah) is included or excluded from the ruling based on its self-subsistence and position in the statement.

Core Idea
Whether 'ila' includes its limit depends on the limit's self-subsistence and its position in the statement.

This lesson explores the Hanafi usul principle governing the particle 'ila' (to/until) when it marks a ghayah (limit). The distinction hinges on whether the limit is self-subsisting (qa'im bi nafsihi) or not, and whether it appears at the beginning of the statement. Understanding this helps correctly derive rulings from Quranic texts such as the verses on wudu and fasting.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three scenarios of ghayah
Classify the limit as self-subsisting (example 1), non-self-subsisting at the beginning (example 2), or non-self-subsisting with doubt/not at the beginning (example 3).
Example 1: 'from this wall to this wall' – wall is self-subsisting. Example 2: 'and your hands to the elbows' – elbows are not self-subsisting and at beginning. Example 3: 'complete the fast until night' – night is not self-subsisting, and there is doubt about its inclusion.
2
Determine inclusion or exclusion for each scenario
Self-subsisting: both starting and ending limits are included. Non-self-subsisting at beginning: the limit is excluded. Non-self-subsisting with doubt: the limit is not included, and the ruling is drawn up to but not including the limit.
Thus, in 'from this wall to this wall', both walls are included. In wudu, elbows are excluded. In fasting, night is not part of the fast.
3
Apply the principle to the Quranic verses
Use the principle to interpret the verses: 'wa aydikum ila al-marafiq' and 'thumma atimmu al-siyama ila al-layl'.
This yields the Hanafi ruling that elbows are not washed and fasting ends before night enters.
4
Contrast with other usul approaches
Note that other schools (e.g., Shafi'i) may generally exclude the limit regardless, but the Hanafi view differentiates based on the nature of the ghayah.
This highlights the importance of the type of ghayah in Hanafi istinbat.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اور ( الی ) انتہائے غایت کیلئے آتا ہے تو اگر غایت قائم بنفسہما ہو یعنی وہ پہلے سے موجود ہو اور اپنے وجود میں منیا کا محتاج نہ ہو تو دونوں غائیں (غایت ابتداء اور غایت انتهاء ) ہوں گی اور اگر وہ قائم نفسمانہ ہوتو پھر اگر جنایت صدر کلام میں واقع ہو تو نایت کا ذکر ما در او کو نکالنے کیلئے ہوگا اور اگر صدر کلام غایت کو شامل نہ ہو یا اس میں شک ہو تو غایت کا ذکر کرنا حکم کو اس تک کھینچنے کیلئے ہوگا۔ لہذا غایت منیا میں داخل نہیں ہو گا تینوں قسم کی مثالیں ترتیب کے ساتھ یہ ہیں۔
(۱) من هذه الحائط الى هذه الحائط
(۲) وايديكم الى المرافق
(۳) ثم اتموا الصيام الى اليل
And 'ila' is used for the endpoint of a limit. So if the limit is self-subsisting, i.e., it already exists and does not need the means for its existence, then both limits (starting limit and ending limit) will be included. And if it is not self-subsisting, then if the limit occurs at the beginning of the speech, mentioning the limit is to expel what is within it. And if the beginning of the speech does not include the limit or if there is doubt, then mentioning the limit is to draw the ruling towards it. Thus, the limit will not enter the thing limited. The three examples in order are:
(1) 'From this wall to this wall'
(2) 'And your hands to the elbows'
(3) 'Then complete the fast until the night.'
Source pages p. 202

Commentary
This passage explains the usul principle regarding the particle 'ila' when it denotes a limit (ghayah). The author distinguishes three scenarios: (1) When the limit is self-subsisting (qa'im bi nafsihi), like a wall, the limit is included in the ruling because it is an existing entity that can encompass both the beginning and end. (2) When the limit is not self-subsisting and appears at the beginning of the statement, it functions to exclude the limit, as in the Quranic verse about washing hands to the elbows — the elbows are not washed because the ghayah is used to expel what is beyond? Actually, the ruling is that the limit is excluded so the elbows are not included. (3) When there is doubt or the limit is not included in the beginning, like fasting until night, the limit is used to pull the ruling to that point, meaning fasting ends at night but night is not included in the fast. This principle is applied in Hanafi usul to interpret legal texts involving limits.

Key Terms
غایت (ghayah): The endpoint or limit of a scope; a point up to which a ruling applies or from which it begins.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the verse 'thumma atimmu al-siyama ila al-layl' (Quran 2:187), according to the passage, is the night included in the fasting?
A) Yes, it is included
B) No, it is excluded
C) It is included only in Hanafi school
D) It depends on the intention

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, the inclusion or exclusion of a ghayah marked by 'ila' depends on whether the limit is self-subsisting and its position in the statement.

Adding Divorce to a Place: Immediate Effect vs Conditional Intent
Rule on immediate divorce when attached to a place unless verb is implied

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that attaching a place to a divorce utterance gives immediate effect unless a verb is implied, and distinguish this from explicit conditional divorce.

Core Idea
Divorce attached to a place is immediate; only an implied verb makes it conditional.

This passage from Nur al-Anwar explains a key linguistic-legal rule: when a husband says 'You are divorced in Makkah', the divorce takes effect immediately at the utterance, not upon reaching Makkah. The default in Hanafi usul is immediate effect unless the context indicates a conditional intent through an implied verb. The distinction affects when divorce occurs and whether it can be revoked.

Guided Path
1
Identify the utterance and its added element
The husband says 'You are divorced in Makkah' – the divorce is attached to a place (Makkah).
The phrase is a statement of location, not a condition.
2
Apply the default Hanafi rule
In Hanafi usul, when a divorce is added to a place, the default interpretation is literal: the place is the location where the utterance is made, so divorce occurs immediately (halan).
This is based on the principle that al-asl fi al-kalam al-haqiqah (the default in speech is literal meaning).
3
Identify the exception
If a verb is implied (e.g., 'if you go to Makkah'), the phrase becomes conditional. The divorce then occurs only when the condition is fulfilled.
The exception is flagged by the phrase 'illa an yudmira al-fi‘l fa-yasira bi-ma‘na al-shart'.
4
Contrast with explicit conditional
When the husband explicitly says 'If you enter Makkah, you are divorced', it is clearly conditional. The rule confirms that explicit conditions override the default immediate effect.
This shows the importance of the verb in determining the legal effect.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : واذا اضيف الى مكان يقع حالاً إلا أن يضمر الفعل فيصير بمعنى الشرط.
اور اگر طلاق کی نسبت کسی مکان کی طرف کرے اور مثلا یوں کہے انت طالق في مكة توفى الحال طلاق واقع ہو جائے گی لیکن اگر مصدر کو مقدر مانا جائے تو شرط کے قبیل میں سے ہوگا یا اس نے یوں کہا ان دخلت مكة فانت طالق تو مکہ میں داخل ہونے کے ساتھ طلاق واقع ہو جائے گی۔ اگر مکہ میں داخل نہ ہو تو طلاق بھی نہیں ہوگی۔
His statement: 'And if it is added to a place, it occurs immediately unless the verb is implied, then it becomes in the meaning of condition.'
And if he relates divorce to a place, for example, he says 'You are divorced in Makkah', divorce occurs immediately. But if the infinitive is considered implied, then it will be of the type of condition. Or if he says 'If you enter Makkah, you are divorced', then divorce occurs upon entering Makkah. If he does not enter Makkah, then divorce will not occur.
Source pages p. 203

Commentary
This passage explains the rule for divorce when mentioned with a place. If a husband says 'You are divorced in Makkah', the divorce takes effect immediately at the time of utterance, because the phrase is seen as a statement of location, not a condition. However, if an implicit verb (like 'if you go') is understood, then it becomes a conditional divorce. The text also contrasts with an explicit conditional sentence: 'If you enter Makkah, you are divorced' — here divorce only occurs upon entering Makkah. The default in Hanafi fiqh is immediate effect unless a conditional intent is clearly established.

Key Terms
حالا (halan): Immediately, at the moment of utterance.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) When she enters Makkah

Key Takeaway
Divorce attached to a place is immediate unless a verb is implied.

Nouns of Time and Place: 'Qabla' and 'Ba'da' in Talaq Counting
Rulings on the zarf nouns 'qabla' and 'ba'da' and their contradictory effect in divorce counting

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi usul rule regarding 'qabla' and 'ba'da' to determine the number of divorces in a pronouncement and identify when pronoun attachment changes the interpretation.

Core Idea
In Hanafi divorce counting, 'qabla' and 'ba'da' have opposite effects: one triggers two, two triggers one.

This lesson examines how the placement of temporal particles 'qabla' (before) and 'ba'da' (after) in divorce statements affects the number of divorces counted. The Hanafi school derives these rulings from the linguistic function of these particles as zarf nouns, and the principle that in ambiguous expressions, the default interpretation follows the literal meaning unless context dictates otherwise.

Guided Path
1
Identify the linguistic category
Recognize that 'qabla', 'ba'da', and 'ma'a' are zarf nouns indicating temporal or spatial relationships. Their literal meanings are: qabla = before, ba'da = after, ma'a = together.
This classification comes from Arabic grammar and is foundational to their legal interpretation.
2
Determine the default legal effect in divorce
In Hanafi law, when used in divorce pronouncements, these particles affect the number of divorces. Specifically, 'qabla' indicates that the first divorce occurs before the second, while 'ba'da' indicates after. Their effects are opposite: if one divorce occurs with 'qabla', two occur with 'ba'da', and vice versa.
The passage states: 'and their ruling in divorce is opposite to the ruling of qabla'.
3
Analyze the impact of pronoun restriction
When 'qabla' or 'ba'da' is attached to a pronoun (e.g., qablahā, ba'dahā), they function as adjectives modifying the subsequent phrase. This changes the interpretation: they no longer affect the divorce count as separate temporal markers but describe the condition of the divorce.
The passage states: 'when they are restricted by a pronoun, they become an adjective for what follows'.
4
Apply to the given example
The problem: husband says to a non-consummated wife 'You are divorced one qabla one'. Here 'qabla' is not attached to a pronoun, so it retains its temporal function. The default ruling from the rule is that one divorce with 'qabla' yields two divorces total (the first before the second). Therefore, two divorces occur.
The example is incomplete in the text but the principle is clear.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : ومنها اسماء الظروف فمع المقارنة وقبل للتقديم وبعد للتأخير وحكمهما في الطلاق ضد حكم قبل واذا قيدت بالكناية كانت صفة لما بعدها واذا لم تقيد كانت صفة لما قبلها حروف معانی میں سے اسمائے ظروف بھی ہیں ان میں سے ( مع ) مقارنت کیلئے آتا ہے اور ( قبل ) تقدیم کیلئے اور (بعد ) تاخیر کیلئے اور طلاق میں (بعد ) کا حکم ( قبل) کے حکم کا ضد ہے یعنی جس صورت میں ( قبل ) میں ایک طلاق واقع ہوگی (بعد) میں دو واقع ہوں گی اور جس صورت میں ( قبل ) میں دو تو ( بعد ) میں ایک واقع ہوگی۔ اور جب قبل اور بعد کو ضمیر کے ساتھ مقید کیا جائے تو اپنے مابعد کے لئے صفت ہوں گے مثلا اگر کسی نے غیر مدخولہ بیوی سے کہا انت طالق واحدة قلبها واحدة تودو طلاقیں واقع ہونگی اور اگر کہا انت طالق واحدة بعد هار واحدة تو اس صورت میں
His statement: 'And among them are the nouns of containers. So 'ma'a' is for conjunction, 'qabla' for precedence, and 'ba'da' for postponement. And their ruling in divorce is opposite to the ruling of 'qabla'. And when they are restricted by a pronoun, they become an adjective for what follows them, and when not restricted, they are an adjective for what precedes them.'
Among the particles of meaning are also the nouns of containers. Among them, 'ma'a' is for conjunction, 'qabla' for precedence, and 'ba'da' for postponement. And in divorce, the ruling of 'ba'da' is the opposite of the ruling of 'qabla', i.e., in the case where one divorce occurs with 'qabla', two will occur with 'ba'da', and where two occur with 'qabla', one will occur with 'ba'da'. And when 'qabla' and 'ba'da' are restricted by a pronoun, they become adjectives for what follows them. For example, if someone says to his non-consummated wife 'You are divorced one qabla one', then two divorces will occur. And if he says 'You are divorced one ba'da one', then in this case [incomplete]

Commentary
This passage explains the usage of certain nouns of time/place (zarf nouns) in the context of divorce. 'Ma'a' indicates conjunction, 'qabla' indicates precedence, and 'ba'da' indicates postponement. A key point is that 'ba'da' has the opposite legal effect of 'qabla' when counting divorces. For example, if a husband says 'You are divorced one qabla one' (meaning one divorce before another), a specific number of divorces result; if he says 'ba'da', the numbers are reversed. Furthermore, when these words are attached to a pronoun (like qablahā or ba'dahā), they become adjectives describing the following phrase. The example given involves a non-consummated wife (ghayr madkhul biha) where saying 'taliq wahidata qabla wahida' results in two divorces because 'qabla' makes the first conditional? The text is cut off, but the principle is that the placement of these particles changes the number of divorces. This is specific to Hanafi fiqh in interpreting ambiguous divorce statements.

Key Terms
قبل (qabla): A noun of time meaning 'before', used for precedence in a sequence.
بعد (ba'da): A noun of time meaning 'after', used for postponement.

Definition and Types of Azimat in Shariah
Defines Azimat and classifies its four types

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define Azimat and classify its four types using the Hanafi criteria of denial, punishment, and blame.

Core Idea
Azimat is the original Shariah ruling legislated without excuse, divided into fard, wajib, sunnah, and nafal.

In this lesson, we explore the foundational concept of Azimat (determination) in Hanafi usul al-fiqh. Azimat represents the default ruling in Shariah, unmodified by any excuse. The author first defines Azimat, then divides it into four categories based on the consequences of denial and abandonment. Understanding this classification is crucial for correctly identifying the legal weight of any act of worship.

Guided Path
1
Define Azimat
Identify the definition of Azimat as the original ruling legislated without any excuse, covering both commands and prohibitions.
Azimat is the default; rukhsah is exceptional.
2
List the four types
Recall that Azimat is divided into fard, wajib, sunnah, and nafal.
These are the only categories under Azimat.
3
Analyze the criterion for distinction
Examine the commentator's method: first check if denial makes one a disbeliever (fard); if not, check if abandonment incurs punishment (wajib); if not, check if abandonment incurs blame (sunnah); otherwise nafal.
This is a stepwise threshold test.
4
Define Fard specifically
Note that fard is defined as a ruling established by definitive evidence (qat'i) that admits no increase or decrease, free from doubt.
Examples given: iman and the five pillars.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل مشروعات کے بیان میں
احکام مشروعہ کی بنیادی طور پر دو قسمیں ہیں (۱) رخصت (۲) عزیمت ما اور بہ کی قسم اول عزیمت :
صاحب کتاب رحمہ اللہ نے اولا عزیمت کی تعریف اور اسکے بعد اسکی تقسیم فرمائی ہے۔
عزیمت کی تعریف
عزیمت احکام میں اصل ہے۔ اور اسکی مشروعیت کسی عارض کی بناپر نہیں ہوا کرتی خواہ اسکا تعلق فعل
سے ہو جیسے ما مورات شرعیہ یا ترک فعل سے ہو جیسے منہیات شرعیہ۔
عزیمت کی تقسیم:
عزیمت کی ابتداء کل چار قسمیں ہیں۔ (۱) فرض (۲) واجب (۳) سنت (۴) نفل وجه حصر بطرز شارح:۔۔۔۔ عزیمت کا منکر کا فر کہلائے گا یا نہیں ۔ اگر اس کا منکر کا فر کہلائے گا تو وہ فرض ہے اگر اس کا منکر کا فرنہیں کہلاتا تو اس کی دو صورتیں ہیں۔ اسکا تارک موجب عقاب ہے یا نہیں ۔ اگر ہے تو واجب ہے اگر تارک موجب عقاب نہیں تو دو حال سے خالی نہیں یا تو اس کا تارک ملامت کا مستحق ہوگا یا نہیں۔ اول سنت اور ثانی نفل ہے ۔
(۱) فرض کی تعریف
فرض
وهى مالا يحتمل زيادة ولا نقصاناً بالدليل لا شبهة فيه كالايمان ولاركان الاربعة وهى الصلوة والزكوة والصم والحج.
Section on the explanation of legislated matters. The legislated rulings are fundamentally of two types: (1) Rukhsah (concession) and (2) Azimat (determination). We shall first discuss the first type: Azimat. The author, may Allah have mercy on him, first defines Azimat and then its division. Definition of Azimat: Azimat is the original in rulings. Its legislation is not based on any excuse, whether it pertains to an act, like commanded acts, or to the abandonment of an act, like prohibited acts. Division of Azimat: Azimat is initially of four types: (1) Fard, (2) Wajib, (3) Sunnah, (4) Nafal. The method of limitation according to the commentator: Whether the denier of Azimat will be called a disbeliever or not. If his denier is called a disbeliever, then it is Fard. If his denier is not called a disbeliever, then there are two possibilities: is its abandoner subject to punishment or not? If yes, then it is Wajib. If the abandoner is not subject to punishment, then there are two cases: either the abandoner deserves blame or not. The first is Sunnah and the second is Nafal. (1) Definition of Fard: Fard is that which does not allow of increase or decrease, by evidence, without any doubt in it, like faith and the four pillars: prayer, zakat, fasting, and hajj.
Source pages p. 253

Commentary
This passage introduces the classification of Shariah rulings into two categories: Azimat (determination) and Rukhsah (concession). The focus here is on Azimat. The author first defines Azimat as the original ruling that is legislated without any excuse, covering both commands and prohibitions. Then he divides Azimat into four types: Fard, Wajib, Sunnah, and Nafal. The criterion for this division is based on the consequence of denial (takfir) and abandonment ('iqab and blame). If denying a ruling makes one a disbeliever, it is Fard. If not, but abandoning it incurs punishment, it is Wajib. If the abandoner is not punished but deserves blame, it is Sunnah. If no blame, it is Nafal. The passage ends with the definition of Fard: a ruling that is established by definitive evidence, admits no increase or decrease, and is free from doubt. Examples are given: faith (iman) and the four pillars of Islam: prayer, zakat, fasting, and hajj. This follows the Hanafi usul al-fiqh tradition where Fard is equivalent to what is necessary by definitive proof, while Wajib is necessary by speculative proof.

Key Terms
عزیمت (azimat): Original ruling in Shariah that is legislated without any excuse, whether pertaining to acts or abandonment.
فرض (fard): A ruling established by definitive evidence (qat'i), denial of which leads to disbelief; admits no increase or decrease.
واجب (wajib): A ruling whose abandoner is subject to punishment but whose denier is not a disbeliever.
سنت (sunnah): A ruling whose abandoner deserves blame but not punishment.
نفل (nafal): A recommended act whose abandoner neither deserves punishment nor blame.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Hanafi usul, what is the criterion to distinguish fard from wajib in the category of azimat?
A) Fard is based on the Quran, wajib on hadith.
B) Fard is that whose denier is called a disbeliever; wajib is that whose abandoner is subject to punishment but denier is not a disbeliever.
C) Fard is that which cannot be abrogated; wajib can be abrogated.
D) Fard is the original ruling; wajib is a concession.

Key Takeaway
Azimat is the default ruling, classified into fard, wajib, sunnah, and nafal based on the effects of denial, punishment, and blame.

Azimah and the Fourfold Classification of Obligatory Rulings
Defining and classifying 'azimah into four types based on evidence and consequence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the definition of azimah and classify a given fiqh ruling into one of the four categories (fard, wajib, sunnah, nafl) using the Hanafi method based on evidence and consequence.

Core Idea
Azimah is the default Shari'ah ruling; its four categories are determined by evidence certainty and the consequence of abandonment.

This passage introduces the foundational concept of azimah—the original ruling of Shari'ah unaffected by excuses. The author presents a logical method to classify any legislated command into fard, wajib, sunnah, or nafl based on two criteria: the nature of the evidence (definitive or ambiguous) and the consequence for the abandoner (punishment or blame). This framework is essential for understanding the hierarchy of obligations in the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Understand the definition of azimah
Note that azimah is the original ruling, not due to any impediment, covering both commands and prohibitions. It is contrasted with rukhsah (concession).
The passage states: 'عزیمت احکام میں اصل ہے۔ اور اسکی مشروعیت کسی عارض کی بناپر نہیں ہوا کرتی'
2
Identify the two criteria for classification
The first criterion: does the evidence have ambiguity (shubhah)? If not, it is fard. If yes, then check the consequence: is the abandoner punished? If yes, it is wajib. If not punished but blamed, it is sunnah. If neither, it is nafl.
This logical tree is explained in the Urdu text: 'وجه حصر بطرز شارح'
3
Apply the criteria to derive the four categories
Trace the logical tree: denier of the ruling becomes disbeliever -> fard. If denier not disbeliever, then check if abandoner is sinful -> wajib. If not sinful, then check if abandoner is blameworthy -> sunnah. Otherwise nafl.
The passage explicitly follows this sequence.
4
Relate to the textual definitions
The passage then defines each category. For fard and wajib, note the specific examples: faith and five pillars for fard; zakat al-fitr and sacrifice for wajib.

احکام مشروعہ کی بنیادی طور پر دو قسمیں ہیں (۱) رخصت (۲) عزیمت ما اور بہ کی قسم اول عزیمت :
صاحب کتاب رحمہ اللہ نے اولا عزیمت کی تعریف اور اسکے بعد اسکی تقسیم فرمائی ہے۔
عزیمت کی تعریف
عزیمت احکام میں اصل ہے۔ اور اسکی مشروعیت کسی عارض کی بناپر نہیں ہوا کرتی خواہ اسکا تعلق فعل
سے ہو جیسے ما مورات شرعیہ یا ترک فعل سے ہو جیسے منہیات شرعیہ۔
عزیمت کی تقسیم:
عزیمت کی ابتداء کل چار قسمیں ہیں۔ (۱) فرض (۲) واجب (۳) سنت (۴) نفل وجه حصر بطرز شارح:۔۔۔۔ عزیمت کا منکر کا فر کہلائے گا یا نہیں ۔ اگر اس کا منکر کا فر کہلائے گا تو وہ فرض ہے اگر اس کا منکر کا فرنہیں کہلاتا تو اس کی دو صورتیں ہیں۔ اسکا تارک موجب عقاب ہے یا نہیں ۔ اگر ہے تو واجب ہے اگر تارک موجب عقاب نہیں تو دو حال سے خالی نہیں یا تو اس کا تارک ملامت کا مستحق ہوگا یا نہیں۔ اول سنت اور ثانی نفل ہے ۔
(۱) فرض کی تعریف
فرض
وهى مالا يحتمل زيادة ولا نقصاناً بالدليل لا شبهة فيه كالايمان ولاركان الاربعة وهى الصلوة والزكوة والصم والحج.
فرض کا حکم:
فرض سے علم یقینی اور عمل قطعی کا فائدہ دیتا ہے۔ لہذا ابلا عذر ترک کرنے والا فاسق ہوگا یہ فرض کے موجب برائے عمل قطعی ہونے کا ثمر ہے اور علم کا ثمرہ یہ ہے کہ اس کا منکر کا فر ہے۔
(۲) واجب
واجب کی تعریف
ماثبت بدليل فيه شبهة كالعام المخصوص والمجمل والخبر
الواحد كصدقة الفطر والأضحية .
واجب کا حکم:
اس سے علم یقینی کا فائدہ حاصل نہیں ہوتا بلکہ یہ علم فلنی کا فائدہ دیتا ہے۔ لہذا اس کا منکر کا فرنہیں البتہ فاسق ہے جبکہ باعتبار عمل یہ فرض ہی کی طرح ہے بلکہ اسکا نام فرض عملی بھی ہے ۔ اگر کوئی شخص واجب کی توہین کرے تو کافر ہو جائے گا ۔ لان اهانة الشريعة كفر ائمہ ثلاثہ کے ہاں واجب مستقل تم نہیں ۔

Section on the explanation of legislated matters.
Legislated rulings are fundamentally of two types: (1) Concession (rukhsah) and (2) Determination (azimah). ... The first type is 'azimah:
The author (may Allah have mercy on him) first defined 'azimah and then divided it.
Definition of 'azimah: 'Azimah is the original in rulings. Its legislation is not due to any impediment, whether it pertains to an act, like the commanded matters of Shari'ah, or the abandonment of an act, like the prohibited matters of Shari'ah.
Division of 'azimah: 'Azimah initially has four categories: (1) Fard, (2) Wajib, (3) Sunnah, (4) Nafl. The method of enumeration according to the commentator: ... [Regarding] 'azimah, will its denier be called a disbeliever or not? If its denier is called a disbeliever, then it is fard. If its denier is not called a disbeliever, then there are two possibilities. Is its abandoner subject to punishment or not? If yes, then it is wajib. If the abandoner is not subject to punishment, then two cases remain: either its abandoner is deserving of blame or not. The first is sunnah and the second is nafl.
(1) Definition of Fard: It is that which does not admit of increase or decrease by evidence, and there is no ambiguity in it, like faith and the five pillars: prayer, zakat, fasting, and pilgrimage.
Ruling of Fard: Fard provides certain knowledge and decisive action. Therefore, one who abandons it without excuse is a sinner. This is the result of fard being decisive in action, and the result of its knowledge is that its denier is a disbeliever.
(2) Wajib: Definition: That which is established by evidence containing some ambiguity, like the general text that has been specified, the ambiguous text, and the solitary report, such as zakat al-fitr and sacrifice.
Ruling of Wajib: It does not provide certain knowledge, but rather provides probable knowledge. Therefore, its denier is not a disbeliever, though he is a sinner, while in terms of action it is like fard; indeed its name is 'practical fard'. If someone insults a wajib act, he becomes a disbeliever, because insulting the Shari'ah is disbelief. According to the three imams, wajib is not an independent [category] – [it is not?].
(3) Sunnah: Definition lexically: path and way, whether good or bad. Technical definition: The path followed in religion besides fard and wajib.
Ruling of Sunnah: A Muslim will be asked to establish it, as evidenced by Allah's saying: 'Take what the Messenger gives you and refrain from what he forbids you.'
Source pages p. 254

Commentary
This passage is a definition and classification of the primary rulings of Shari'ah (azimah) as opposed to concessions (rukhsah). The author begins by stating that all legislated rulings are either azimah or rukhsah, and then focuses on azimah. He explains that azimah is the original ruling not affected by any excuse or impediment, whether it commands an action or prohibits one. Then he divides azimah into four categories based on a logical method: first, look at the evidence—if it is definitive (qat'i) and unambiguous, the ruling is fard; if the evidence has some ambiguity (like a general text that has been specified or a solitary hadith), it is wajib. Then, for the remaining categories, consider the consequence of abandonment: if the abandoner is punished (in the Hereafter), it is wajib; if not punished but blameworthy, it is sunnah; if neither punished nor blamed, it is nafl. The author then defines each category. Fard is established by definitive evidence without any doubt, e.g., the five pillars. Its knowledge is certain and its action is obligatory; its denier becomes a disbeliever and its abandoner without excuse is a sinner. Wajib is established by evidence with some ambiguity (shubhah), like the general text (amm) that has been specified, or a solitary hadith (khabar wahid). It gives probable knowledge (zann), not certainty, so its denier is not a disbeliever but is a sinner. However, in terms of action, it is like fard (obligatory to perform). If someone intentionally insults a wajib act, they become a disbeliever because it is an insult to the Shari'ah. Note that according to the three imams (Abu Hanifa's companions), wajib is not considered a separate category distinct from fard in terms of obligation; actually fard and wajib are synonymous in their view. But in the Hanafi madhhab, we distinguish. Sunnah is defined technically as the path followed in religion besides fard and wajib; its establishment is recommended and the Muslim is encouraged to follow it, as per the Quranic verse to take what the Messenger gives.

Key Terms
عزیمت (azimah): The original ruling of Shari'ah that is not affected by any impediment or excuse; it is the default category of rulings.
فرض (fard): A ruling established by definitive evidence with no ambiguity; its denier is a disbeliever and its intentional abandoner is sinful.
واجب (wajib): A ruling established by evidence containing some ambiguity (shubhah); its denier is not a disbeliever but its abandoner is sinful.
سنت (sunnah): A recommended act that is not fard or wajib; its abandoner is not sinful but is blameworthy.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which category of 'azimah applies when the denier is not a disbeliever but the abandoner is sinful?
A) Fard
B) Wajib
C) Sunnah
D) Nafl

Key Takeaway
Azimah is the default ruling; its four categories are derived by checking evidence certainty and consequence of abandonment, with fard from definitive evidence and wajib from ambiguous evidence.

Fard vs Wajib: The Hanafi Distinction Based on Evidence and Consequence
Defining and classifying 'azimah into four types based on evidence and consequence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish fard and wajib in the Hanafi school by comparing their evidential basis (qat'i vs. shubhah) and the legal consequences for the denier and abandoner.

Core Idea
Fard is proven by definitive evidence, its denier becomes a disbeliever; wajib is proven by probable evidence, its denier is sinful but not a disbeliever.

This lesson delves into the first two categories of azimah: fard and wajib. The passage provides precise definitions and rulings, highlighting that fard is based on evidence with no ambiguity (shubhah), such as the Quranic verses on the five pillars, while wajib is based on evidence with some ambiguity, like a solitary hadith or a general text that has been specified. The practical consequence is that the denier of fard commits disbelief, whereas the denier of wajib does not, though both are sinful for abandonment. This distinction is unique to the Hanafi school and affects fatwa and classification.

Guided Path
1
Review the definition of fard
Fard is that which does not admit increase or decrease, with no ambiguity in the evidence. Examples: faith and the five pillars (prayer, zakat, fasting, hajj).
Text: 'فرض وهى مالا يحتمل زيادة ولا نقصاناً بالدليل لا شبهة فيه'
2
Review the definition of wajib
Wajib is established by evidence containing shubhah, such as a general text that has been specified (amm makhsus), an ambiguous text (mujmal), or a solitary report (khabar wahid). Examples: zakat al-fitr and udhiyah (sacrifice).
Text: 'ماثبت بدليل فيه شبهة كالعام المخصوص والمجمل والخبر الواحد'
3
Analyze the consequences
Fard gives certain knowledge (ilm yaqini) and decisive action (amal qat'i); its denier is a disbeliever. Wajib gives probable knowledge (zann); its denier is not a disbeliever but is sinful. However, insulting a wajib act leads to disbelief because it insults the Shari'ah.
Text: 'فرض سے علم یقینی اور عمل قطعی کا فائدہ دیتا ہے... اس کا منکر کا فر ہے' and 'واجب... یہ علم ظنی کا فائدہ دیتا ہے... اس کا منکر کافرنہیں'
4
Note the intra-school and inter-school differences
The passage notes that according to the 'three imams' (likely the other schools), wajib is not an independent category; they consider all obligations as fard. In the Hanafi school, the distinction is maintained.
Commentary clarifies that the three imams refer to the other major mujtahids who do not separate fard and wajib.
5
Apply the distinction
Use the criteria to classify a ruling as fard or wajib: check the evidence for ambiguity. If the evidence is definitive (e.g., Quran mutawatir), it is fard. If it has ambiguity (e.g., khabar wahid), it is wajib.
Practice with examples like the five daily prayers (fard) vs. witr (wajib).

Note that according to the three imams (Abu Hanifa's companions), wajib is not considered a separate category distinct from fard in terms of obligation; actually fard and wajib are synonymous in their view. But in the Hanafi madhhab, we distinguish. Sunnah is defined technically as the path followed in religion besides fard and wajib; its establishment is recommended and the Muslim is encouraged to follow it, as per the Quranic verse to take what the Messenger gives.

Key Terms
عزیمت (azimah): The original ruling of Shari'ah that is not affected by any impediment or excuse; it is the default category of rulings.
فرض (fard): A ruling established by definitive evidence with no ambiguity; its denier is a disbeliever and its intentional abandoner is sinful.
واجب (wajib): A ruling established by evidence containing some ambiguity (shubhah); its denier is not a disbeliever but its abandoner is sinful.
سنت (sunnah): A recommended act that is not fard or wajib; its abandoner is not sinful but is blameworthy.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the consequence for the denier of a wajib act?
A) He becomes a disbeliever.
B) He is not a disbeliever but is a sinner.
C) He is not a disbeliever and not a sinner.
D) He is a disbeliever only if he insults the act.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, fard is from definitive evidence with certain knowledge, wajib from probable evidence; the distinction affects whether the denier is deemed a disbeliever.

The Hanafi Definition of Fard: Knowledge and Action
Defines Fard and its binding legal consequences

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define Fard in Hanafi usul and distinguish the consequences of abandoning it without excuse from denying its obligatory nature.

Core Idea
Fard is defined by certain knowledge and definitive action: abandonment without excuse makes one a fasiq; denial makes one a kafir.

In Hanafi usul al-fiqh, the term 'Fard' denotes an obligation established by a definitive proof. This lesson unpacks its two-fold consequence: one for the one who abandons it without excuse, and another for the one who denies its obligatory nature. Understanding this distinction is essential for correctly classifying acts and their legal weight.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two fruits (thamarat) of Fard
The passage states that Fard brings about 'certain knowledge' and 'definitive action'. Recognize these as the two outcomes: one related to belief (knowledge) and one related to practice (action).
The 'fruit' imagery is common in classical usul.
2
Apply the fruit of action
Because Fard requires definitive action, abandoning it without a valid excuse makes one a fasiq (sinner). This is the practical legal consequence.
This is a sin, not necessarily disbelief.
3
Apply the fruit of knowledge
Because Fard gives certain knowledge, denying that it is obligatory makes one a kafir (disbeliever).
Denial here means rejecting the obligation itself, not just failing to act.
4
Contrast with other categories (optional expansion)
Unlike Fard, Wajib in Hanafi is established by a probable (zanni) proof; therefore, denying a Wajib does not lead to kufr, only abandonment without excuse is sinful.
This distinction is unique to the Hanafi school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فرض کا حکم: ہ علم یقینی اور عمل قطعی کا فائدہ دیتا ہے۔ لہذا ابلا عذر ترک کرنے والا فاسق ہوگا یہ فرض کے موجب برائے عمل قطعی ہونے کا ثمر ہے اور علم کا ثمرہ یہ ہے کہ اس کا منکر کا فر ہے۔
The ruling of Fard: It gives the benefit of certain knowledge and definitive action. Therefore, the one who abandons it without excuse is a sinner. This is the fruit of Fard being definitive in terms of action, and the fruit of knowledge is that its denier is a disbeliever.
Source pages p. 255

Commentary
This passage explains the legal ruling of Fard (obligatory) in Hanafi usul. Fard is established through a definitive proof (dalil qat'i), giving certain knowledge. Consequently, abandoning it without a valid reason makes one a sinner (fasiq). Denying its obligatory nature constitutes disbelief (kufr). This distinction separates Fard from lesser categories.

Key Terms
فرض (fard): That which is established by a definitive proof (dalil qat'i) and requires definitive action.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi definition of Fard, what is the consequence for someone who denies its obligatory nature?
A) They become a fasiq (sinner).
B) They become a kafir (disbeliever).
C) They are not punished.
D) They must repeat the act.

Key Takeaway
Fard is established by certain knowledge and requires definitive action; abandonment without excuse makes one a fasiq, denial makes one a kafir.

The Hanafi Concept of Wajib: Obligation with Probable Evidence
Defines Wajib and its distinct legal effect compared to Fard

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to DEFINE Wajib according to Hanafi usul, IDENTIFY its basis in zanni dalil, and DISTINGUISH its legal effect from Fard in terms of both belief and action.

Core Idea
Wajib is obligatory but zanni — denial does not make you a disbeliever, but insulting it does.

In Hanafi usul, not all obligations are equal. While Fard is established by certain evidence (qat'i), Wajib is established by probable evidence (zanni). This distinction has major implications: the denier of a Wajib is not a kafir, but a fasiq. However, in terms of action, Wajib carries the same binding force as Fard — and insulting a Wajib is an insult to the Shariah itself. In this lesson, we will dissect the definition of Wajib and its ruling, and we will see why the other three Hanafi Imams (Abu Yusuf, Muhammad, and Zufar) reject this distinction.

Guided Path
1
Identify the defining features of Wajib
What proofs establish a Wajib? Name the three types of ambiguous evidence mentioned. Note the examples given (Sadaqat al-Fitr, Udhiya).
2
Analyze the epistemological weight
Compare the knowledge (ilm) derived from Wajib vs. Fard. How does this affect the status of the denier?
3
Distinguish the practical obligation
Despite the weaker evidence, what is the ruling on performing a Wajib? In what sense is it called 'practical Fard'?
4
Examine the boundary case: insult
Why does insulting a Wajib lead to kufr? What principle governs this?
5
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Why do the three other Imams reject an independent category of Wajib? What does this imply for practical application?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واجب واجب کی تعریف: ماثبت بدليل فيه شبهة كالعام المخصوص والمجمل والخبر الواحد كصدقة الفطر والأضحية . واجب کا حکم: اس سے علم یقینی کا فائدہ حاصل نہیں ہوتا بلکہ یہ علم فلنی کا فائدہ دیتا ہے۔ لہذا اس کا منکر کا فرنہیں البتہ فاسق ہے جبکہ باعتبار عمل یہ فرض ہی کی طرح ہے بلکہ اسکا نام فرض عملی بھی ہے ۔ اگر کوئی شخص واجب کی توہین کرے تو کافر ہو جائے گا ۔ لان اهانة الشريعة كفر ائمہ ثلاثہ کے ہاں واجب مستقل تم نہیں ۔
Wajib: Definition: That which is established by a proof containing some ambiguity, like the general qualified, the ambiguous, and the solitary report, such as Sadaqat al-Fitr and Udhiya. Ruling of Wajib: It does not give certain knowledge but rather gives probable knowledge. Therefore, its denier is not a disbeliever (kafir), but rather a sinner (fasiq). However, in terms of action, it is like Fard; indeed, it is called practical Fard. If someone insults a Wajib, he becomes a disbeliever, because insulting the Shariah is disbelief. According to the three Imams, Wajib is not an independent category.
Source pages p. 255

Commentary
This passage defines Wajib and its ruling in Hanafi usul. It is established by a proof with some ambiguity (shubha), such as a general text that has been qualified, an ambiguous (mujmal) text, or a solitary hadith (khabar wahid). Examples include Sadaqat al-Fitr (obligatory charity at the end of Ramadan) and Udhiya (sacrificial animal). Unlike Fard, Wajib gives only probable (zanni) knowledge, so its denier is not a disbeliever but a sinner. However, in terms of obligation to perform, it is equivalent to Fard; hence it is sometimes called 'practical Fard' (fard 'amali). But insulting a Wajib is considered insulting the Shariah, which is disbelief. The passage notes that according to the other three Imams (Abu Yusuf, Muhammad, Imam Zufar — the three of the Hanafi school besides Abu Hanifa), Wajib is not a separate category; they equate it with Fard.

Key Terms
واجب (wajib): That which is established by a proof containing ambiguity (shubha), e.g., khabar wahid.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the legal status of Sadaqat al-Fitr?
A) Fard
B) Wajib
C) Sunnah
D) Mubah

Key Takeaway
Wajib is obligatory but its denial does not cause kufr; only insulting it does.
