Definition and Ruling of Sunnah in Hanafi Usul
Defines Sunnah, its ruling, and the Hanafi position on its usage

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to: (1) state the Hanafi technical definition of Sunnah, (2) apply the definition to distinguish Sunnah from fard, wajib, and nafl, (3) explain the difference between Sunan al-Huda and Sunan Zawa'id, and (4) evaluate the Shafi'i objection to applying 'sunnah' to non-Prophetic practices.

Core Idea
Sunnah: a path in religion, neither fard nor wajib; its emphasized form (Mu'akkadah) makes abandoner blameworthy.

This lesson introduces the Hanafi definition of Sunnah as a category of religious practice distinct from fard and wajib. We will examine the ruling that Muslims are called upon to perform it, the proof from the Quran, and the precise boundaries of the definition. The passage also presents a key Hanafi position: the term 'sunnah' can legitimately refer to practices of the Companions, unlike the Shafi'i view. Finally, we divide Sunnah into two types: Sunan al-Huda (emphasized) and Sunan Zawa'id (non-emphasized), based on whether abandonment incurs blame.

Guided Path
1
Grasp the linguistic and technical definitions
Start with the linguistic meaning of 'sunnah' (way, path, good or bad). Then internalize the technical definition: 'the path followed in religion without being fard or wajib.' This is the precise Hanafi formulation.
Note that the definition excludes nafl because 'is called upon', excludes fard and wajib by explicit statements.
2
Identify the ruling and its proof
The ruling: a Muslim is called upon (yutlabu) to establish Sunnah, but not with the same binding force as fard or wajib. The proof is the Quranic verse 'wa ma atakumu al-rasulu fakhudhuhu' (59:7).
This verse is used to support the obligation of following the Prophet's commands, including his sunnah practices.
3
Analyze the definition's restrictions (fawa'id al-quyud)
The definition has three parts: (1) 'is called upon' excludes nafl, (2) 'without making it fard' excludes fard, (3) 'without obligation' excludes wajib. Ensure you see how each restriction carves out the category.
This three-part exclusion is a classic example of hadd (definition) analysis in usul.
4
Distinguish between Sunan al-Huda (Mu'akkadah) and Sunan Zawa'id
Sunan al-Huda: abandoner is blameworthy (e.g., congregational prayer). Sunan Zawa'id: no blame (e.g., following the Prophet in dress). Understand the practical difference in fiqh gravity.
The definition and ruling in the passage primarily applies to Sunan al-Huda, but the division covers both types.
5
Examine the Shafi'i objection to Hanafi usage of 'sunnah'
Hanafis apply 'sunnah' to practices of Companions (e.g., 'sunnah of the two shaykhs'). Shafi'is require explicit attribution to the Prophet or specification of the source. Compare their proofs: Hanafis cite hadith 'man sanna sunna hasana'; Shafi'is cite Sa'id ibn al-Musayyib's statement. Understand the thamarah (practical consequence): in fatwa, a Hanafi can say 'it is sunnah' based on a Companion's practice; a Shafi'i cannot unless it is the Prophet's sunnah or they specify.
The text sides with the Hanafi position, noting that the Shafi'i evidence actually supports the Hanafi view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
سنت کی تعریف : اندی معنی طریقہ اور راستہ خواہ اچھا ہو یا برا۔ اصلاحی تعریف: الطريقة المسلوكة في الدين بغير الفرض والواجب . سنت کا حکم : ۔ مسلمان سے اس کے قائم کرنے کا مطالبہ کیا جائے گا جس پر دلیل اللہ تعالی کا یہ قول ہے: وما آتاكم الرسول فخذوه وما نهاكم عنه فانتهوا . فوائد قیود: (1) ان يطالب: یہ فصل اول ہے جس سے نفل نکل گیا۔ (۲) من غير افتراض : فصل ثانی ہے۔ جس سے فرض خارج ہو گیا۔ (۳) ولا وجوب : یہ فصل ثالث ہے جس سے واجب نکل گیا۔ اب تعریف جامع لافرادہ اور مانع عن غیرہ ہو گئی۔ و لكـن قـــالــوا ان هذا التعريف الخ شارخ وضاحت کر رہے ہیں کہ مذکورہ حکم اور تعریف کا مصداق صرف سنن ھدی (سنت مؤکدہ) ہے البتہ آنے والی تقسیم سن صدی کے علاوہ زوائد کی بھی ہے۔ نکته ضروریہ: احناف کے ہاں سنت کا اطلاق غیر نبی کے طریقے پر بھی درست ہے لقوله عليه السلام من سن سنة فله اجرها واجر من عمل بھا ۔ شوافع اس اطلاق کو بلا اضافت جائز نہیں مانتے بلکہ صراحت ضروری ہے مثلا یوں کہے هذه سنة الشيخين وهذه سنة ابی بکر رضی الله عنهم . ان کی دلیل سعید بن مسیب کا قول ہے ما دون الثلاث من الدية لا ينصف وهو السنة یہاں سعید بن مسیب کا اشارہ سنت نبی کی طرف نہیں بلکہ حضرت سید زید بن ثابت رضی اللہ منھم کے قول کی طرف ہے۔ سنت کی پہلی تقسیم : سنت کی دو قسمیں ہیں (۱) سنن ھدی یا سنت مؤکدہ اور (۲) زوائد أو سنت غیر مؤکدہ (1) سنن ھدی کی تعریف:۔ جس کا مطالبہ اس طور پر ہو کہ اس کا تارک ملامت اور عتاب کا مستوجب ہو مثلا جماعت ، اذان، اقامت۔ (۲) سنن زوائد کی تعریف:۔ جس کا ترک کرنے والا ملامت یا عناب کا مستحق نہ ہو ستاد لباس ، قیام اور قعود وغیرہ عادات میں اتباع نبوی والا الله
Definition of Sunnah: Linguistically, way and path, whether good or bad. Technical definition: The path followed in religion without being fard or wajib. Ruling of Sunnah: The Muslim is called upon to establish it, as evidenced by the saying of Allah the Exalted: 'And whatever the Messenger gives you, take it, and whatever he forbids you, abstain from it.' Benefits of the restrictions: (1) 'is called upon': this first clause excludes nafl. (2) 'without making it fard': second clause excludes fard. (3) 'and without obligation': third clause excludes wajib. Thus the definition becomes comprehensive of its individuals and exclusive of others. But they said that this definition's application (the commentator explains) is only to Sunan al-Huda (emphasized Sunnah); however, the upcoming division includes both Sunan al-Huda and Zawa'id (supererogatory). Important note: Among the Hanafis, the term 'Sunnah' is also validly applied to the way of other than the Prophet, based on his saying: 'Whoever establishes a good sunnah, for him is its reward and the reward of those who act upon it.' The Shafi'is do not consider this application permissible without an addition; rather, explicit specification is necessary, e.g., saying 'this is the sunnah of the two shaykhs' or 'this is the sunnah of Abu Bakr (may Allah be pleased with them).' Their evidence is the saying of Sa'id ibn al-Musayyib: 'Whatever is less than one-third of the blood money is not subject to oath, and that is the sunnah.' Here Sa'id ibn al-Musayyib's reference is not to the sunnah of the Prophet but to the saying of Sayyidina Zayd ibn Thabit (may Allah be pleased with them). First division of Sunnah: Sunnah is of two types: (1) Sunan al-Huda or Mu'akkadah (emphasized) and (2) Zawa'id or Ghayr Mu'akkadah (non-emphasized). (1) Definition of Sunan al-Huda: That which is called for in such a way that its abandoner deserves blame and reproach, e.g., congregation, adhan, iqamah. (2) Definition of Sunan Zawa'id: That which its abandoner does not deserve blame or reproach, like following the Prophet in matters of dress, standing, sitting, and other habits.
Source pages p. 255

Commentary
This passage provides a comprehensive Hanafi treatment of Sunnah. It begins with the linguistic and technical definitions: technically, Sunnah is a religious practice that is neither fard nor wajib. The ruling is that Muslims are called upon to perform it, supported by the Quranic verse (59:7). The commentators analyze the definition's restrictions: 'is called upon' excludes nafl (voluntary), 'without making it fard' excludes fard, and 'without obligation' excludes wajib. However, they clarify that this definition and its ruling apply specifically to Sunan al-Huda (emphasized Sunnah, also called Sunnah Mu'akkadah). The upcoming division will also cover Zawa'id (non-emphasized Sunnah). An important Hanafi position is that the term 'sunnah' can also refer to practices of the Companions and the Rightly-Guided Caliphs, based on the hadith: 'Whoever establishes a good sunnah...' The Shafi'is disagree, holding that 'sunnah' without addition refers only to the Prophet's practice; otherwise, one must specify the source. They cite Sa'id ibn al-Musayyib's statement '...and that is the sunnah' meaning the practice of Zayd ibn Thabit, not the Prophet. Finally, the passage divides Sunnah into two: (1) Sunan al-Huda (Mu'akkadah) — abandoning them is blameworthy, e.g., congregation, adhan, iqamah; (2) Sunan Zawa'id — not blameworthy, e.g., following the Prophet in dress, sitting, etc.

Key Terms
سنة (sunnah): A religious practice that is neither fard nor wajib; includes both Mu'akkadah and Ghayr Mu'akkadah.
سنة مؤكدة (sunnah mu'akkadah): Emphasized Sunnah whose abandoner is blameworthy, e.g., congregational prayer, adhan, iqamah.
سنن زوائد (sunan zawa'id): Non-emphasized Sunnah; following the Prophet in habitual actions; abandoner not blameworthy.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What distinguishes Sunan al-Huda (Mu'akkadah) from Sunan Zawa'id?
A) Sunan al-Huda are based on the Quran, Zawa'id on hadith.
B) Abandoning Sunan al-Huda deserves blame; abandoning Zawa'id does not.
C) Sunan al-Huda are obligatory; Zawa'id are recommended.
D) Sunan al-Huda are for men; Zawa'id for women.

Key Takeaway
The definition and ruling of Sunnah in Hanafi usul are carefully delimited to exclude fard, wajib, and nafl, and the term can apply to practices of the Companions, but the degree of blame depends on whether the sunnah is emphasized (Mu'akkadah) or not.
